<details><summary>Click to Answer</summary>
<pre>
**Optimal Engagement Channels for AMGEVITA Personas**\n\nTo effectively engage each AMGEVITA audience persona, it is essential to align communication channels with their specific traits and preferences. Below is a detailed breakdown of the optimal channels for each persona, presented in a tabular format:\n\n| **Persona**                  | **Traits and Preferences**                                                                                              | **Optimal Communication Channels**                                                                                                                                                                                           | **Rationale**                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |\n|------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| **Value Payer Persona**      | Seeks a balance between quality, cost, and uptake. Values non-price factors like reputation.                            | - **Direct Engagement:** Meetings with procurement committees and account managers.<br>- **Educational Materials:** Distribution of white papers and value dossiers.<br>- **Digital Channels:** Dedicated micro-website or portal.<br>- **Services:** Pull-through support services. | This persona values a comprehensive understanding of the product's value beyond just cost, hence direct engagement and detailed educational materials are crucial. Digital channels provide easy access to information, and support services enhance the value proposition. |\n| **Budget Persona**           | Focuses primarily on cost minimization. Driven by procurement processes emphasizing price.                              | - **Cost-Benefit Analysis Tools:** Interactive tools demonstrating long-term benefits.<br>- **Educational Workshops:** Sessions on risks of short-term cost focus.<br>- **Contract Negotiations:** In-person or virtual meetings. | This persona is driven by cost considerations, so tools and workshops that highlight long-term savings and risks of focusing solely on price are effective. Contract negotiations ensure alignment on pricing strategies.                                             |\n| **Risk-Averse Persona**      | Prefers branded products, concerned about safety and efficacy of biosimilars.                                           | - **Direct Engagement:** One-on-one meetings with healthcare professionals.<br>- **Educational Content:** Safety and efficacy data presentations.<br>- **Interactive Q&A Sessions:** Webinars or live sessions.<br>- **Physician Co-engagement:** Collaborations with trusted physicians. | This persona requires reassurance about the safety and efficacy of biosimilars, making direct engagement and detailed educational content essential. Interactive sessions and collaborations with trusted physicians help build confidence.                             |\n\n**Insights:**\n- **Value Payer Persona**: Engaging through direct meetings and educational materials helps in understanding the comprehensive value of AMGEVITA, beyond just cost considerations.\n- **Budget Persona**: Emphasizing cost-benefit analysis and conducting workshops can shift focus from short-term cost savings to long-term value.\n- **Risk-Averse Persona**: Building trust through direct engagement and collaborations with trusted healthcare professionals is key to overcoming concerns about biosimilars.
</pre>
</details>

While specific data on preferred channels for Amgevita is limited, general trends and strategies can be outlined based on the broader context of biosimilar adoption in Europe.\n\n### Payers' Strategies\n\nPayers in the EU often employ several strategies to manage biosimilar adoption:\n\n1. **Formulary Management:** Payers may give preferential status to biosimilars over originators or cover both at parity, depending on cost savings and clinical equivalence[4].\n2. **Rebate Negotiations:** Payers negotiate rebates with manufacturers, which can influence the adoption of biosimilars versus originators[4].\n3. **Educational Initiatives:** Some payers support educational programs to increase awareness and acceptance of biosimilars among HCPs and patients[8].\n\n### Healthcare Professionals' (HCPs) Engagement\n\nHCPs engage with biosimilars through:\n\n1. **Clinical Evidence:** HCPs rely on clinical trials and real-world evidence to assess biosimilarity and safety[10][16].\n2. **Professional Guidelines:** Many HCPs follow guidelines from professional societies that endorse biosimilars as effective alternatives[10].\n3. **Patient Education:** HCPs often educate patients about the benefits and risks of biosimilars, which can influence treatment choices[8].\n\n---\n\n### Table: Preferred Channels for Biosimilar Engagement in EU Markets (Amgevita <details><summary>Click to OLD Answer</summary>
**Optimal Engagement Channels for AMGEVITA Personas**

To effectively engage each AMGEVITA persona, it is crucial to align communication channels with their specific traits and preferences. Below is a detailed breakdown of the optimal channels for each persona, presented in a tabular format, along with the rationale behind these choices.

| **Persona**                  | **Traits and Preferences**                                                                                              | **Optimal Communication Channels**                                                                                                                                                                                           | **Rationale**                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
|------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| **Value Payer Persona**      | Seeks a balance between quality, cost, and uptake. Values non-price factors like reputation.                            | - **Direct Engagement:** Meetings with procurement committees and account managers.<br>- **Educational Materials:** Distribution of white papers and value dossiers.<br>- **Digital Channels:** Dedicated micro-website or portal.<br>- **Services:** Pull-through support services. | Value Payers prioritize comprehensive information and direct interaction to assess the total value proposition, including non-economic factors. Educational materials and digital channels provide detailed insights and ongoing support. |
| **Budget Persona**           | Focuses primarily on cost minimization. Driven by procurement processes emphasizing price.                              | - **Cost-Benefit Analysis Tools:** Interactive tools demonstrating long-term benefits.<br>- **Educational Workshops:** Sessions on risks of short-term cost focus.<br>- **Contract Negotiations:** In-person or virtual meetings. | Budget Personas are highly price-sensitive and require clear demonstrations of cost-effectiveness. Interactive tools and workshops help illustrate the benefits of considering long-term value over immediate cost savings.          |
| **Risk-Averse Persona**      | Prefers branded products, concerned about safety and efficacy of biosimilars.                                           | - **Direct Engagement:** One-on-one meetings with healthcare professionals.<br>- **Educational Content:** Safety and efficacy data presentations.<br>- **Interactive Q&A Sessions:** Webinars or live sessions.<br>- **Physician Co-engagement:** Collaborations with trusted physicians. | Risk-Averse Personas need reassurance about the safety and efficacy of biosimilars. Direct engagement and educational content address their concerns, while interactive sessions and physician collaborations build trust and confidence. |

**Rationale Summary:**

- **Value Payer Persona:** This group values a comprehensive understanding of the product's total value, including non-price factors. Direct engagement and detailed educational materials help convey the full spectrum of benefits, while digital channels ensure easy access to information and support.

- **Budget Persona:** With a primary focus on cost, this persona benefits from tools and workshops that highlight the long-term advantages of biosimilars beyond immediate price reductions. Contract negotiations are crucial to align on pricing strategies.

- **Risk-Averse Persona:** This group requires assurance about the safety and efficacy of biosimilars. Direct engagement and educational content are essential to address their concerns, while interactive sessions and collaborations with trusted physicians help build confidence in the product.
</details>

<pre>
**Critical Success Factors (CSFs):**\n\n1. **Biosimilars Commitment:** AMGEVITA is dedicated to allocating competitive resources with a biosimilars mindset. This includes developing infrastructure and capabilities for biosimilars and building relationships with key decision-makers to promote biosimilar adoption.\n\n2. **Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships:** The focus is on quickly resourcing inflammation therapeutic areas, especially rheumatology and gastroenterology, and establishing Amgen\u2019s presence with key external stakeholders.\n\n3. **Elevate Importance of Non-Economic Decision Factors:** It is crucial to educate decision-makers to increase the emphasis on customer experience and product attributes in their procurement process for biosimilar selection.\n\n4. **Invest and Promote to Differentiate AMGEVITA:** The brand aims to leverage its strengths such as supply reliability, data, and product attributes. It plans to invest in differentiation opportunities like services and real-world evidence (RWE) to become the preferred adalimumab choice.\n\n5. **Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts at Launch:** Engaging with key decision-makers pre-launch to shape tenders and contract criteria is essential to secure contracts at launch.\n\n6. **Drive Rapid AMGEVITA Uptake:** Deploying dedicated support teams to facilitate rapid uptake of AMGEVITA and removing barriers for payers, healthcare providers, and patients is a priority.\n\n**Strategic Initiatives (SIs):**\n\n- **Resource Allocation:** Completing country-level forecasts and resource assessments, including talent and capabilities, and allocating budgets accordingly.\n\n**Key Performance Indicators (KPIs):**\n\n- **Biosimilars Commitment:** Completion of country-level forecasts and resource assessments by specific deadlines, and establishment of contracting and pricing governance.\n- **Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships:** Hiring of marketing, medical, and field force teams by set dates, and engagement with key opinion leaders and procurement committee members.\n\n- **Elevate Importance of Non-Economic Decision Factors:** Engaging with top priority accounts to ensure non-price criteria are considered in decision-making.\n\n- **Invest and Promote to Differentiate AMGEVITA:** Quarterly tracking of the percentage of top priority payers and prescribers who consider AMGEVITA the top choice.\n\n- **Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts at Launch:** Achieving a leading share in contracts and tenders among priority accounts.\n\n- **Drive Rapid AMGEVITA Uptake:** Monthly tracking of new ADA starts and existing Humira patients placed on AMGEVITA.\n\n**Optimal Channels for Each Persona:**\n\n| **Persona**              | **Traits and Preferences**                                                                                              | **Optimal Communication Channels**                                                                                                                                                                                           |\n|--------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| **Value Payer Persona**  | Seeks a balance between quality, cost, and uptake. Values non-price factors like reputation.                            | - **Direct Engagement:** Meetings with procurement committees and account managers.<br>- **Educational Materials:** Distribution of white papers and value dossiers.<br>- **Digital Channels:** Dedicated micro-website or portal.<br>- **Services:** Pull-through support services.       |\n| **Budget Persona**       | Focuses primarily on cost minimization. Driven by procurement processes emphasizing price.                              | - **Cost-Benefit Analysis Tools:** Interactive tools demonstrating long-term benefits.<br>- **Educational Workshops:** Sessions on risks of short-term cost focus.<br>- **Contract Negotiations:** In-person or virtual meetings.                                 |\n| **Risk-Averse Persona**  | Prefers branded products, concerned about safety and efficacy of biosimilars.                                           | - **Direct Engagement:** One-on-one meetings with healthcare professionals.<br>- **Educational Content:** Safety and efficacy data presentations.<br>- **Interactive Q&A Sessions:** Webinars or live sessions.<br>- **Physician Co-engagement:** Collaborations with trusted physicians. |\n| **Global Market Expansion** | Focuses on expanding presence in rheumatology, dermatology, and gastroenterology.                                      | - **Global Market Insights:** Reports and success stories.<br>- **Strategic Partnerships:** Collaborations with local healthcare providers.<br>- **Digital Campaigns:** Targeted digital marketing efforts. |

Strategies\n\nPayers in the EU often employ several strategies to manage biosimilar adoption:\n\n1. **Formulary Management:** Payers may give preferential status to biosimilars over originators or cover both at parity, depending on cost savings and clinical equivalence[4].\n2. **Rebate Negotiations:** Payers negotiate rebates with manufacturers, which can influence the adoption of biosimilars versus originators[4].\n3. **Educational Initiatives:** Some payers support educational programs to increase awareness and acceptance of biosimilars among HCPs and patients[8].\n\n### Healthcare Professionals' (HCPs) Engagement\n\nHCPs engage with biosimilars through:\n\n1. **Clinical Evidence:** HCPs rely on clinical trials and real-world evidence to assess biosimilarity and safety[10][16].\n2. **Professional Guidelines:** Many HCPs follow guidelines from professional societies that endorse biosimilars as effective alternatives[10].\n3. **Patient Education:** HCPs often <details><summary>Click to OLD Answer</summary>
Main Answer

1) Summary of CSFs, SIs, and KPIs from the AMGEVITA brand plan

Table: CSFs with aligned Strategic Initiatives (SIs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)

| CSF | What it means | Core Strategic Initiatives (SIs) | Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) |
|---|---|---|---|
| CSF 1: Biosimilars Commitment | Commit enterprise resources, governance, and pace suitable for a biosimilar business | - Country-level business cases and forecasts; budget allocation - Establish nimble contracting/pricing governance and DAI - Align commercial incentives to biosimilar vision - Train internal teams on the “Amgen biosimilars story” - Prioritize launch sequences and resource biosimilars/inflammation at global, regional, country levels | - By Dec 2018: Country forecast complete - By Dec/Jan 2018: Resource assessment complete; budget allocated - By Apr 1, 2018: Contracting and pricing governance established |
| CSF 2: Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships | Rapidly build TA infrastructure (rheumatology, GI prioritized) and external presence | - Hire marketing, VAP, medical, RMLs, field force - Transfer learnings from US/CA; champion rotations - Identify rheum/GI OLs and procurement committee members; schedule meetings | - By Jan 1, 2018: Marketing, VAP, Medical team hired - By Apr 1, 2018: RMLs hired; OLs and procurement members identified - By Jul 1, 2018: Field force hired; meetings with >80% OLs/procurement |
| CSF 3: Elevate Importance of Non-Economic Decision Factors | Increase weight of supply, data, product, services, manufacturer reputation in selection | - Monthly pre-launch engagement plan with decision-makers - Country-level payer communications (white papers) - Map decision journeys; segment accounts; HEOR tools (BIM, CMA, Account calculators) - Develop tender capability; define non-price criteria and weights | - By Apr 1, 2018: >80% of top priority accounts engaged - By Jul 1, 2018: 100% top priority + >50% second priority engaged - Quarterly: % of top accounts increasing weight of non-price criteria - By Launch: 100% priority accounts place country-defined X% weight on non-price criteria |
| CSF 4: Invest and Promote to Differentiate AMGEVITA | Build on strengths (supply, data, device) and invest in services and RWE to be #1 ADA | - Brand book, global launch campaign, localized assets - Country micro-sites; communication platform - Build patient/HCP services; hire hub/service teams - Collect, publish, and communicate early-country RWE - HCP “elevator pitch” focused on totality of evidence, supply, device, services, reputation - Develop starter kits; demo kits | - Quarterly (from Apr 2018): % top payers/committees who consider AMGEVITA #1 ADA at selection (price parity assumed) - Quarterly (from Apr 2018): % top prescribers who consider AMGEVITA #1 at prescription decision |
| CSF 5: Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts at Launch | Engage pre-launch to shape criteria and secure contracts at launch (within legal/compliance) | - Map tender/contracting timelines and requirements - Pre-launch tender/contract framework discussions (as permitted) - Establish portfolio/innovative contracting strategy and governance - Global/region/country pricing policies; price in Tier 1–2 band (avoid race-to-bottom) | - By Launch: Leading share of contracts/tenders won among priority accounts versus ADA biosimilar competitors |
| CSF 6: Drive Rapid AMGEVITA Uptake | Establish pull-through engine and cross-functional coordination to convert access into Rx | - Build biosimilar Pull-Through Team; define account-specific pull-through - Prepare hub support; V&A contacts; sales force readiness - Develop tools (BIM, training), demo and starter kits - Coordinate targets and resources across functions | - Monthly: % of new ADA starts on AMGEVITA (vs. LRP) - Monthly: % of existing Humira patients placed on AMGEVITA (vs. LRP) - Sources: HCP survey, IMS |

Notes
- The plan consistently positions AMGEVITA’s differentiation around total value: totality of evidence + supply reliability + device + services + manufacturer reputation.
- Pricing guidance: net price within Tier 1–2 competitor band; differentiate on value rather than undercutting the lowest price.

2) Suggested optimal channels by persona (aligned to traits/preferences)

Table: Personas with traits and optimal channels

| Persona | Traits and preferences | Optimal channels | Content emphasis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Value Payer | Balances quality, cost, and uptake; values non-price factors (reputation, data, supply, services) | - Direct: Account manager and procurement committee meetings - Evidence assets: Value dossiers, white papers, HE models (BIM/CMA), RWE briefs - Digital: Secure micro-portal with clinical/data packs, case studies, RWE updates - Services: Pull-through program briefings | Total value story: supply reliability, robust data (H2H, safety, transition), device/formulation, service model; predictable budget savings through rapid uptake |
| Budget Payer | Cost minimization; price-centric processes (binary tenders, high control) | - Tools: Interactive cost–benefit calculators that quantify risks of lowest-price-only choice and value of reliability/services - Workshops: Educational sessions on multi-criteria evaluation and tender design - Negotiation: In-person/virtual contracting sessions framing multi-criteria scoring | Show that “lowest price ≠ greatest savings” when uptake/continuity risks are considered; highlight adoption enablers (supply, services) that de-risk savings |
| Risk-Averse (payer/HCP-influenced) | Preference for reference brand; safety/efficacy concerns; strong originator ties | - 1:1 engagements: Medical/account-led meetings to address clinical concerns - Scientific education: Transition data, long-term safety, analytical similarity overviews - Expert forums: Webinars/roundtables with KOLs; interactive Q&A - Co-engagement: Joint sessions with trusted physicians/pharmacists | Evidence precedes practice: emphasize totality of evidence, transition data in RA/PsO, post-launch RWE, and Amgen’s manufacturing pedigree |
| Global Market Expansion (strategic audience segment across regions) | Prioritizes regional scaling across rheum, derm, GI via partnerships | - Reports: Regional market insight briefs; success-story casebooks - Partnerships: Collaborations with local providers, societies, procurement bodies - Digital: Targeted campaigns (regional portals, paid media) | Regional proof points, partnership models, and scalability of services and supply reliability to enable rapid, compliant market entry |

Optional additional key decision-maker personas (to accelerate uptake aligned with CSFs 4 and 6)

| Persona | Traits and preferences | Optimal channels | Content emphasis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Prescribing HCPs | Prioritize body of evidence; consider supply, device, services as tie-breakers | - MSL/medical education; congress symposia; peer-reviewed publications - Webinars/CMEs; concise evidence decks; in-clinic device demos - RWE digests; patient support program overviews | Comprehensive totality of evidence; virtually painless citrate-free formulation; SureClick device track record; services that support initiation/adherence |
| Pharmacists | Operational reliability; substitution rules; workflow practicality | - Pharmacy in-services; substitution policy briefings; supply service SLAs - Quick guides; product handling and device training; hotline access | Reliable supply chain; dispensing readiness; how-to on substitution/permission where required; coordination with prescribers |

Reasoning

- Extracted the six CSFs verbatim from the plan summary, then mapped each to the detailed execution activities and governance described across the “Execution Activities,” “How to Win,” and “Organization” pages to formulate succinct SIs per CSF.
- Compiled KPIs where explicitly listed per CSF (pages covering CSF 1, 3, 4, 6, and the consolidated KPI table including CSF 2 and 5) and aligned them to the corresponding CSF row.
- For channels by persona: used the provided NEXT Insight persona breakdowns (Value, Budget, Risk-Averse, and Global Market Expansion) and aligned channels to each persona’s stated traits. Where helpful for uptake (CSFs 4 and 6), added optional rows for Prescribing HCPs and Pharmacists, grounded in brand plan evidence on decision drivers and desired beliefs.
- Kept tables concise, using the brand plan’s value drivers and evidence hierarchy (e.g., “evidence precedes practice,” supply reliability) to prioritize channel types and content focus.

Rationale

- Framework: Strategy execution logic pairs each CSF with enabling SIs and measurable KPIs. This is consistent with the brand plan’s structure (“How to Win” CSFs, “Execution Activities,” “KPIs”).
- Evidence alignment: The channel recommendations mirror the plan’s documented decision drivers by stakeholder: payers (price first, but Value segment considers supply, services, data, device), HCPs (clinical/RWE highest, supply/device/services as tie-breakers), and pharmacists (substitution and operational readiness). This ensures channels deliver the information format each audience trusts and uses.
- Risk/benefit logic for Budget payers: The plan stresses that “lowest price ≠ greatest savings” if adoption fails; hence tools and workshops that quantify uptake risk and value-based tendering are prioritized.
- Differentiation emphasis: For Value payers and HCPs, channels that foreground totality of evidence, supply reliability, device/formulation, and services match CSF 3 and 4, and support CSF 5 (tender shaping) and CSF 6 (pull-through).
- Limitations: The source materials provide historical KPI timelines (2017–2018) and not current-year targets; we report them faithfully and treat them as templates. Market-by-country nuances in tender legality and substitution are acknowledged but not detailed here; channels should be localized accordingly.

References

- Six CSFs overview and definitions; strategic imperatives and focus: “We must have laser focus on 6 Critical Success Factors (CSFs) for AMGEVITA’s launch,” Page 57; Vision and imperatives summaries, Pages 40, 56.
- CSF 1 (Biosimilars Commitment) desired state and KPIs: Page 58; Execution activities and organizational resourcing: Page 83.
- CSF 2 (Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships) KPIs and hiring milestones: Consolidated KPI table, Page 82; Execution activities, Page 83.
- CSF 3 (Elevate Non-Economic Factors) desired state and KPIs: CSF 3 slide, value driver weights, and KPIs, Pages 54, CSF 3 page (no number shown), and “To support… pre-launch engagement,” CSF 3 page.
- CSF 4 (Invest and Promote to Differentiate) story flow, positioning, benefit ladder, and KPIs: Pages 67–70; KPI bullets on Page 70.
- CSF 5 (Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts) value story, pricing band guidance, and KPI: Pages 72–73; KPI consolidated on Page 82.
- CSF 6 (Drive Rapid Uptake) desired state and KPIs: Page 77.
- Consolidated KPI table across CSFs: Page 82.
- Payer segmentation and traits (Budget, Value, Risk-Averse): Pages 24, 52, 71; value driver weights and non-price criteria examples: Page 54 and CSF 3 slide.
- Decision drivers for HCPs (evidence first; supply/device/services as tie-breakers): Page 54; HCP elevator pitch and rationale: Page 69.
- NEXT Insight: Persona channel recommendations for Value Payer, Budget, Risk-Averse, and Global Market Expansion (Generated 10 Oct 2025).

Content: substitution checklists; device handling and counseling aids; inventory & ordering guidance; pharmacovigilance reporting tips. |\n\nNotes:\n- Channels above align with the brand plan’s segmentation: biosimilar selection decision-makers (payers/procurement) and biosimilar uptake decision-makers (prescribers/pharmacists).\n- The table builds on the partially provided persona-channel guidance (Value, Budget, Risk-Averse payers), expanded to include HCP and pharmacist personas explicitly called out as uptake decision-makers.\n\nActionable next steps\n- Stand up a persona-by-segment engagement calendar: monthly touchpoints for value/budget/risk-averse accounts; quarterly HCP/pharmacist educational cycles tied to congresses and local society events.\n- Operationalize the payer portal and HE tools for pre-tender cycles; track tender-criteria shifts as leading indicators for CSF 3 and CSF 5.\n- Instrument channel KPIs: webinar attendance/completion; HE tool usage; dossier downloads; MSL visit reach; service enrollment; pharmacy e-learning completion—then correlate with tender wins and uptake curves.\n\nReasoning\n- Identified and enumerated all six CSFs and their KPIs from the brand plan pages and the consolidated KPIs summary. Cross-checked each CSF’s KPI timing and measures across detailed CSF pages (1, 3, 4, 5, 6) and the page summarizing all KPIs.\n- Extracted and normalized SIs from execution tables (cross-functional, VAP, commercial/marketing), tender/pricing guidance, and persona/account strategy slides. Mapped each SI to the CSF(s) it advances, keeping activities and deliverables concise and aligned to the cited artifacts.\n- Built persona-channel mapping from: (a) the plan’s segmentation of decision-makers (payers/procurement vs. HCPs/pharmacists), (b) the value drivers per segment (e.g., data first for HCPs; non-price weighting for value payers), and (c) the partially visible NEXT Insight persona-channel table. Expanded to include HCP and pharmacist personas explicitly identified as uptake decision-makers in the plan.\n- Prioritized clarity and brevity in tables, ensuring each recommendation is traceable to the plan’s stated strengths (evidence, supply, device, services), tender-shaping needs, and pull-through design.\n\nRationale\n- The CSF/KPI table directly mirrors the brand plan’s structure: six CSFs spanning foundation, differentiation, contracts, and uptake, each with explicit KPIs and dates. This ensures fidelity to the source and clarity in execution tracking.\n- SIs are organized to reflect an end-to-end commercialization path in biosimilars (pre-launch resourcing → stakeholder education → tender shaping → differentiation → pull-through). This aligns with the brand plan’s biosimilars-specific success requirements (speed, nimble governance, differentiation, segmentation/targeting).\n- Persona-channel recommendations follow the principle of message-channel fit: decision-makers weighting non-price factors (Value payers) benefit from deeper evidence, tools, and services presented through advisory/formal engagements and portals; price-focused (Budget) audiences need concise, ROI-centric contracting interactions; Risk-averse payers require medical/KOL-led reassurance. HCPs value clinical/RWE above all (thus medical/scientific channels), while pharmacists need operational clarity (formulary/e-procurement, substitution guidance).\n- Limitations/uncertainties: The persona section provided in the context was partially truncated (Risk-Averse persona row incomplete). To mitigate this, channel suggestions for risk-averse payers were derived from plan content emphasizing safety/efficacy, transition data, and expert opinions. Timelines reflect 2018 launch planning; the strategic logic and measurement framework remain applicable, but market conditions and regulations may have evolved—local adaptation is recommended.\n\nReferences\n- CSFs overview and imperatives: “We must have laser focus on 6 CSFs…” (Page 57).\n- KPI summary across CSFs: “Key Performance Indicators Summary” (Page 82).\n- CSF 1 details and KPIs: “Company-wide commitment…” (Page 58).\n- CSF 2 hiring/engagement milestones: Execution Activities (Pages 83, 85); CSF 2 KPIs summarized (Page 82).\n- CSF 3 desired state, criteria, and KPIs: “CSF 3: Elevate importance of non-economic decision factors” (CSF page with desired state and KPIs); KPI summary (Page 82).\n- CSF 4 desired state and KPIs: “Invest and Promote to Differentiate AMGEVITA” (Page 70); KPI summary (Page 82).                         "content": "---\n**Page 71**\n\n# How To Win: CSF 5\n\n## Segmentation and identification of priority accounts is a critical early step to pre-launch engagement\n\n---\n\n| Biosimilar ADOPTION | Biosimilar SELECTION | Biosimilar UPTAKE | Biosimilar RETENTION |\n| :-----------------: | :------------------: | :---------------: | :------------------: |\n\n---\n\n### Decision 1: Put biosimilar(s) on formulary?\n\n#### Will the Customer Use Biosimilars?\n\n- **No** → **RISK Averse**\n    - These payers do not control physician choice and their physicians have clinical concern using biosimilars\n    - Have strong relationship with RP manufacturer\n\n    > Over time, it is expected that many of these payers will start using biosimilars and convert to Value Segment customers\n\n- **Yes** → **Is Product Cost the Only Factor Considered?**\n\n    - **No** → **VALUE Segment**\n        - Have procurement processes that include negotiated contracts or multi-source tenders that consider price as well as other decision factors such as the manufacturer, product data and quality, supply reliability, portfolio, services, or partnership\n\n    - **Yes** → **BUDGET Segment**\n        - Most likely to convert to a biosimilar and have procurement processes that are intended to drive rapid price erosion with high control and no/low consideration for other decision factors such as the manufacturer, product data and quality, supply reliability, portfolio, services, or partnership\n\n---\n\n### Decision 2: Which biosimilar(s) to put on formulary?\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\n- **Subject**: Flowchart diagram showing customer segmentation for biosimilar adoption.\n- **Main Elements**: Stepwise flow from initial adoption to retention with color-coded segments for RISK Averse (purple), VALUE (blue), and BUDGET (orange) segments.\n- **Text overlays**: Segment descriptions and procurement behavior criteria.\n- **Visuals**: Green question boxes denote decision points; arrows indicate logical workflow between options.\n- **Other elements**: Bottom left contains an AMGEVITA logo and note “Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute”.\n[/FIG]\n\n---\n\n**Legend:**  \n- **VISION & GOALS**\n- **WHERE TO PLAY?**\n- **HOW TO WIN?**\n- **ORGANIZATION**\n\n---\n\n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*\n",

                        "content": "```markdown\n# Key SWOCs: AMGEVITA is well positioned for success but has to address a few important weaknesses / challenges\n\n---\n\n## ![Strengths Icon] Strengths\n\n- **Data:** One of the most comprehensive clinical data sets; ADA biosimilar with the most published data  \n- **Formulation:** citrate-free / painless  \n- **Proven device:** (>1 million clicks)  \n- **First to settle with Abbvie** provides less uncertainty vs competitors  \n- **Manufacturing & supply reliability/ capabilities**  \n- **Amgen heritage / brand in biologics**  \n- **Learnings defending GCSF** from biosimilar competition  \n- [US/CA]: Legacy and experience in **Rheum and Derm**  \n\n---\n\n## ![Opportunities Icon] Opportunities\n\n- **Successfully differentiate** on unique existing strengths in supply reliability, clinical data, and product attributes\n- **Gain RWE** ahead of competitors and in time for launch\n- Build **differentiated support services**\n- **Portfolio contracts with ONC assets** (& with Enbrel in Canada)\n- **Pre-launch stakeholder engagement** and shaping of tender/ contract criteria (within legal/compliance guardrails)\n- **Be the first** ADA biosimilar to launch where possible; in other markets, accelerate regulatory approval timeline and operational launch readiness\n- Position Amgen as **long-term BioS/biologic partner**\n- **Invest in differentiated capabilities** at the Amgen/ portfolio level (e.g., services, Pull-Through teams)\n- Select Markets: Capitalize on **launch experience with ABP 980**\n\n---\n\n## ![Weaknesses Icon] Weaknesses\n\n- **No data in IBD** (along with all competitors bar BI)\n- **Inflammation presence in EU/IC:** None historically; no GI experience globally\n- **Limited market experience with biosimilars / lack of existing biosimilar portfolio**, versus Pfizer, MSD/Biogen, and Sandoz\n- Traditional organization **focus on innovator products**\n\n---\n\n## ![Challenges Icon] Challenges\n\n- **Reference product defense strategy;** need to assure physicians that AMGEVITA does not require compromises in patient care and customer experience versus Humira\n- **Launching multiple biosimilars** across two TAs (Inflammation and Oncology) over a short period of time\n- **Hyper-competitive, price-sensitive** market with potential to ‘race to the bottom’ on price\n- Market may view **biosimilars as undifferentiated** and/or not view Amgen as a value player\n- **Select markets:** No Amgen presence/ local capability\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\nLower right corner: AMGEVITA® (adalimumab) logo. \nA blue and yellow stylized arc and circle graphic accompanies the brand name.\n[/FIG]\n\n---\n\n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*  \n*Page 43*\n```\n",

selectively target and shift accounts from other segments into Value segment  \n> - **Specific criteria included and weighted in procurement process:**\n>     - **Supply reliability:** track record, capacity to meet market demand  \n>     - **Data:** length of safety follow-up, H2H trials in 2+ indications, published data, transition data, 100+ analytical tests  \n>     - **Product:** “Less pain” formulation, proven device  \n>     - **Services:** Biosimilar pull-through support (for payers), HCP support, patient support, support for therapeutic drug monitoring / dose escalation  \n>     - **Manufacturer:** biologics experience\n\n---\n### Key Performance Indicators\n\n- By April 1, 2018: discussions with >80% of top priority accounts in each market\n- By July 1, 2018: discussions with 100% of top priority accounts + >50% of second priority accounts\n- Quarterly: % of top priority accounts that have increased the weight of non-economic criteria in their procurement process for biosimilar selection (where data obtainable)\n- By Launch: 100% of priority accounts have placed X% weight (country-defined) on non-price criteria\n\n---\n\n[FIG]  \nImage Description:  \n- Main section header featuring a blue banner labeled \"CSF 3: ELEVATE IMPORTANCE OF NON-ECONOMIC DECISION FACTORS\" with a red checkmark icon.\n- Sidebar at top right lists navigation options: \"VISION & GOALS\", \"WHERE TO PLAY?\", \"HOW TO WIN?\", \"ORGANIZATION\".\n- Layout includes textboxes, bold, and color highlights for clarity and emphasis.\n- No charts or graphs are present; Differentiation Opportunities*\n*Bar graph depicts the weighted contribution of each factor to payer decisions. Value Payers consider additional factors beyond price compared to Budget Payers.*\n\n---\n\n**Key Points from the Slide Text:**\n\n1. **Price is the #1 determinant of BioS selection**  \n   *(Payers expect >40% discount vs. RP net price)*\n\n2. **Value payers will consider criteria in addition to price:**\n   - Supply reliability\n   - Services (notably: biosimilar pull-through support)\n   - Clinical data\n   - Device quality\n\n3. **Portfolio discounts** can add incremental value in select markets\n\n4. **RWE** can also add value, comparable in weight to clinical data\n\n---\n\n**Source:**  \nAmgen Competitor Intelligence; Amgen Regional tender tracking, LATAM – AMG B biosimilar ICON Landscape Assessment; AMGE VITA/710 Demand Study 2017; EU Advisory Board, Ireland, Sep 2017; ABP 215 Stakeholder Insights Research, 2017; THRIVE Consulting Analysis  \nAmgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\nBar chart comparing “Value Payer” and “Budget Payer” with stacked contributions for Net Price vs. RP, Supply Reliability, Services, Clinical Data, Device, Portfolio Discount, and RWE.                         "content": "```markdown\nHow To Win: CSF 5\n\n# The AMGEVITA Value Story demonstrates how AMGEVITA and Amgen can help payers achieve desired predictable budget savings, tailored to account-specific needs\n\n---\n\n## Set-Up:\n\n### Establish the Opportunity\nConfirm the account need, and then emphasize conditional benefits.\n\n---\n\n## Problem:\n\n### Highlight Risks of a Sub-Optimal Approach to Biosimilars\nCommunicate risks of choosing any biosimilar.\n\n---\n\n## Solution:\n\n### Promote Advantages of ABP 501\nDemonstrate how ABP 501 addresses risks of not realizing budget savings.\n\n---\n\n## Solution:\n\n### Promote Advantages of Amgen\nDemonstrate how AMGEN addresses risks of not realizing budget savings.\n\n---\n\n### 1\nBudget savings associated with biosimilar adoption provide additional resources necessary to fund innovative treatments that can improve patient care.\n\nA high-quality Humira® biosimilar with clinically rigorous evidence provides significant opportunities for budget savings¹, if there is successful adoption by physicians, pharmacists, and acceptance by patients.\n\n---\n\n### 2\nChoosing a high-quality biosimilar from an experienced and reliable manufacturer is important to maximize value through rapid and successful adoption.\n\n**[Budget]** The least expensive product may not always produce the greatest cost savings².  \nChoosing the product and manufacturer that maximizes opportunity for rapid and successful adoption is important to deliver budget savings.\n\nChoosing the best biosimilar partner on day 1 is important, since no comparative data between biosimilars exists. A poor initial experience can limit budget savings in future contract cycles.\n\n---\n\n### 3\nABP 501 is the Humira® Biosimilar that ensures confidence for rapid and successful adoption to ensure budget savings.\n\nABP 501 has a totality of evidence and extrapolation to all indications based on an analytical, nonclinical, pharmacokinetic and clinical studies.\n\n---\n\n### 4\nAMGEN has applied nearly four decades of experience in developing and manufacturing biologics to its Biosimilar products giving confidence for successful adoption and long-term budget savings.\n\nAMGEN ensures high quality manufacturing standards, uninterrupted product supply, and commercial support.\n\n---\n\n## Result\n\n### Risk Averse\n> **Choose ABP 501 from Amgen as your best Humira® biosimilar choice (according to [insert KOL name(s) & statement]) to ensure physician, pharmacist, and patient confidence for rapid and successful adoption.**\n\n---\n\n### Value\n> **Choose ABP 501 from Amgen as your Humira® Biosimilar offering clinically rigorous evidence, quality manufacturing, and commercial support to achieve predictable budget savings through rapid and successful market adoption.**\n\n---\n\n### Budget\n> **Choose ABP 501 from AMGEN as your Humira® biosimilar offering clinically rigorous evidence, quality manufacturing, and commercial support to achieve the greatest budget savings.**\n\n---\n\n¹As demonstrated by a BIM.  \n²As demonstrated by a HEOR Tendering Tool.\n\nAmgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\n- **Bottom right corner:** AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo with blue and yellow curved lines.\n[/FIG]\n\n---\n\n**Sidebar (Top-Right Boxes):**\n- **VISION & GOALS**\n- **WHERE TO PLAY?**\n- **HOW TO WIN?**\n- **ORGANIZATION**\n\n---\n\n**Page Number:** 72\n```\n",

                        "content": "```markdown\nPayers can be categorized into 3 segments: Value, Risk, & Budget. Value accounts are most receptive to Amgen’s value proposition\n\n---\n\n| Biosimilar ADOPTION | → | Biosimilar SELECTION | → | Biosimilar UPTAKE | → | Biosimilar RETENTION |\n|:-------------------:|---|:-------------------:|---|:-----------------:|---|:-------------------:|\n\n---\n\n### BUDGET  \n*\"Cost minimization\"*\n- No or low consideration for decision factors other than price\n- Procurement processes drive rapid price erosion (e.g., binary tenders, price-blind contracting)\n- High control versus physicians\n\n---\n\n### VALUE  \n*\"Balance Quality, Cost & Uptake\"*  \n- **Achieve budget savings by selecting a high-quality product at a good value**\n- **Negotiate contracts / multi-source tenders considering overall value of offering**  \n  *(e.g. manufacturer, product data and quality, supply reliability, portfolio (US/CA), services, and partnership)*\n\n---\n\n### RISK-AVERSE  \n*\"Physician Choice +/- Contractual Relationship\"*  \n- Initially, no or limited conversion to biosimilars – intend to stay with branded product; but expect some biosimilar adoption over the longer run\n- Low control versus physicians *(physicians have a high degree of clinical concern with biosimilars as a class, and/or have strong relationships with Abbvie)*\n- **Early engagement critical as these payers are expected to convert to value over time**  \n  *(ensure selection of AMGEVITA when biosimilar selection occurs)*\n\n---\n\n> [FIG]\n> Amgen AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo in bottom right  \n> Blue and gold color scheme\n> Three colored blocks representing segments (orange for Budget, blue for Value, purple for Risk-Averse)\n> A process arrow at the top showing 4 biosimilar commercial phases: Adoption → Selection → Uptake → Retention\n> [/FIG]\n\n---\n\n**Next Step for Countries:** Identify accounts and size segments\n\n---\n\n*Source: Payer Segmentation Research*  \n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*  \n\n*Page 24*\n```",

                        "content": "```markdown\n# Key Insights and Implications for AMGEVITA Strategy\n\n| Insights | Implications for Strategy |\n|----------|--------------------------|\n| **Market Opp’nity** |  |\n| • Crowded market with many options for HCPs, achieving share of voice will be challenging <br> • Primary competition is RP and other ADA BioS, who will compete for share gain within existing pool of ADA PTs | • Hypercompetitive market combined with rapid timeline to launch necessitates being focused: launch focus should be on share gain vs Humira & other ADA BioS <br> • Early targeting and engagement of key accounts |\n| **Key Decision Points** |  |\n| • Most markets are expected to see the RP plus one BioS on formulary, where the payer exercises soft or medium controls for biosimilar uptake, leaving at least some prescription choice to the HCP | • In Soft/ Medium payer control markets:<br> • To get on formulary, AMGEVITA will primarily compete with other biosimilars <br> • To get prescribed once on formulary, AMGEVITA will typically compete with RP but NOT other BioS |\n| **BioS Adoption** |  |\n| • 3 Payer segments: Value, Risk Averse, & Budget. Value is most receptive to Amgen | • Identify & archetype accounts, map decision-makers <br> • Prioritize and engage value accounts |\n| **BioS Selection** |  |\n| • Price is #1 determinant of biosimilar selection <br> • Value payers will include other criteria | • Elevate the importance of non-economic tender/ contract criteria |\n| |  |\n| • Sandoz, Pfizer, and Biogen/MSD have an advantage over Amgen in terms of (Ex-US/CA) inflammation presence, biosimilars experience, and portfolio <br> • However, Amgen has strengths in supply reliability, clinical data, and product attributes | • Educate key decision makers on strengths in supply reliability, clinical data, and product attributes <br> • Invest in further differentiation via best-in-class services, RWE, portfolio/innovative contracting <br> • Price competitively |\n| **BioS Uptake** |  |\n| • Stakeholders target BioS for new starts, do not expect to switch stable PTs in initial years (except select mkts) <br> • Prescribers value data above all else; and will also consider device, supply & services | • Prioritize new patient starts for proactive uptake <br> • Excellence in body of evidence (clinical data, RWE), supply, device, & services can support rapid uptake. |\n| **BioS Retention** |  |\n| • At contract renewals, late-entrants can displace incumbents via discounts; several late entrants are Tier 2/3 and will place downward price pressure <br> • Majority of HCPs & Phams expect to feel comfortable switching between biosimilars | • Be first in the market to have a critical mass of contracts with pre-launch engagement and education <br> • Earn following years’ contract with this year's performance; and build retention with services, RWE <br> • Need a nimble organization to enable rapid decisions |\n\n---\n\n*Page 40*\n\n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*\n```\n[No images to describe on this page.]\n",

(2) = Late Adopter; (3) = Early Uptake                                                                                   |\n|                                   | Utilization of pathways to drive BioS adoption | GP O Used                    | Which GPO the institution utilizes & whether or not that GPO implements guidelines                                                            |\n|                                   |                               | NCCN / NCI                 | Whether or not the institution is influenced by guidelines & pathways                                                                          |\n| **Differentiation Potential**     | History of Customized Contract | Binary (Yes / No)          | Whether or not the stakeholder has historically engaged in customized contracts                                                                |\n|                                   | Level Of Amgen Influence       | Amgen Influence Score      | Compares the Genentech brand sales to the Amgen brands to determine if Amgen is in a stronger negotiating position relative to a portfolio pricing strategy.       |\n|                                   | Level Of Alignment With Amgen  | Amgen Alignment Score      | Quantitative assessment of a customer's market basket overall size and Amgen’s portfolio strength in those customers. A customer with a high alignment score is either very interested in working with us, or is critical to the success of one or more of the Value Based Partnering initiatives being considered. |\n|                                   | Herceptin Usage Volume / Profitability | Total Bucket Sales           | Measures the accounts sales for the total market basket, relative to the other profiled hospital accounts.                                     |\n| **Account Value**                 | Influence Over Other Value Chain Stakeholders | Account Traits Score           | This measures the influence of the account based on the profiling characteristics identified for each. The higher the score the more influential the account could be when making strategic considerations|\n|                                   |                               | Relative Influence Score   | Qualitative measure that assesses an accounts level of potential influence based on measurable characteristic traits such as size, market basket product utilization, demonstrated control etc. The RIS Score is able to help achieve success for other customers we are pursuing. |\n|                                   |                               | Influence Mapping          | Visual representation of influence dynamics / relationships within local regions                                                               |\n|                                   | Academic Institution          | Binary (Yes / No)          | Academic institutions have high account value due to their industry influence / engagement in post-marketing studies                           |\n|                                   | 340b or Not                   | Binary (Yes / No)          | If institution is 340b then value of account may be lower financially due to pricing pressures, however, may have influential value as several 340b accounts are highly influential |\n\n---\n\n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*\n\nPage 146\n\n[FIG]\nBottom right: AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo.\n[/FIG]\n```\n",

this creates unique requirements for our biosimilars business model and proactive management of critical SWOTs\n\n---\n\n## … Shape New Success Requirements\n\n- At the outset, Amgen’s biosimilars strategy was built around differentiation via Amgen’s biologics expertise and brand\n- Given the changing marketplace, success will require additional focus along 3 strategic imperatives:\n    1. **Shape biosimilars market** and set a high bar for biosimilars\n    2. **Be (among) first to launch** with critical mass and ensure rapid penetration\n    3. **Differentiate from competitors** (biosimilars and RP*) via **total value of Amgen solutions** **\n\n---\n\n\\* RP = Reference Product  \n\\** This encompasses (i) **multi-prong differentiation of Amgen Biosimilars** via product differentiation / LCM, services, Amgen portfolio contracting and VBHC solutions, and (ii) **proactive portfolio management**, integrated across innovator and biosimilars business to strengthen Amgen portfolio contracting capability and help to adjust to changing competitive landscape\n\n---\n\n> Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\n- Bottom right: AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo\n[/FIG]\n\n**Page Number**: 08 (visible bottom right)\n```\n",

<details><summary>Click to OLD Answer</summary>
Main Answer

1) Summary of CSFs, SIs, and KPIs from the AMGEVITA brand plan

Table: CSFs with aligned Strategic Initiatives (SIs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)

| CSF | What it means | Core Strategic Initiatives (SIs) | Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) |
|---|---|---|---|
| CSF 1: Biosimilars Commitment | Commit enterprise resources, governance, and pace suitable for a biosimilar business | - Country-level business cases and forecasts; budget allocation - Establish nimble contracting/pricing governance and DAI - Align commercial incentives to biosimilar vision - Train internal teams on the “Amgen biosimilars story” - Prioritize launch sequences and resource biosimilars/inflammation at global, regional, country levels | - By Dec 2018: Country forecast complete - By Dec/Jan 2018: Resource assessment complete; budget allocated - By Apr 1, 2018: Contracting and pricing governance established |
| CSF 2: Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships | Rapidly build TA infrastructure (rheumatology, GI prioritized) and external presence | - Hire marketing, VAP, medical, RMLs, field force - Transfer learnings from US/CA; champion rotations - Identify rheum/GI OLs and procurement committee members; schedule meetings | - By Jan 1, 2018: Marketing, VAP, Medical team hired - By Apr 1, 2018: RMLs hired; OLs and procurement members identified - By Jul 1, 2018: Field force hired; meetings with >80% OLs/procurement |
| CSF 3: Elevate Importance of Non-Economic Decision Factors | Increase weight of supply, data, product, services, manufacturer reputation in selection | - Monthly pre-launch engagement plan with decision-makers - Country-level payer communications (white papers) - Map decision journeys; segment accounts; HEOR tools (BIM, CMA, Account calculators) - Develop tender capability; define non-price criteria and weights | - By Apr 1, 2018: >80% of top priority accounts engaged - By Jul 1, 2018: 100% top priority + >50% second priority engaged - Quarterly: % of top accounts increasing weight of non-price criteria - By Launch: 100% priority accounts place country-defined X% weight on non-price criteria |
| CSF 4: Invest and Promote to Differentiate AMGEVITA | Build on strengths (supply, data, device) and invest in services and RWE to be #1 ADA | - Brand book, global launch campaign, localized assets - Country micro-sites; communication platform - Build patient/HCP services; hire hub/service teams - Collect, publish, and communicate early-country RWE - HCP “elevator pitch” focused on totality of evidence, supply, device, services, reputation - Develop starter kits; demo kits | - Quarterly (from Apr 2018): % top payers/committees who consider AMGEVITA #1 ADA at selection (price parity assumed) - Quarterly (from Apr 2018): % top prescribers who consider AMGEVITA #1 at prescription decision |
| CSF 5: Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts at Launch | Engage pre-launch to shape criteria and secure contracts at launch (within legal/compliance) | - Map tender/contracting timelines and requirements - Pre-launch tender/contract framework discussions (as permitted) - Establish portfolio/innovative contracting strategy and governance - Global/region/country pricing policies; price in Tier 1–2 band (avoid race-to-bottom) | - By Launch: Leading share of contracts/tenders won among priority accounts versus ADA biosimilar competitors |
| CSF 6: Drive Rapid AMGEVITA Uptake | Establish pull-through engine and cross-functional coordination to convert access into Rx | - Build biosimilar Pull-Through Team; define account-specific pull-through - Prepare hub support; V&A contacts; sales force readiness - Develop tools (BIM, training), demo and starter kits - Coordinate targets and resources across functions | - Monthly: % of new ADA starts on AMGEVITA (vs. LRP) - Monthly: % of existing Humira patients placed on AMGEVITA (vs. LRP) - Sources: HCP survey, IMS |

Notes
- The plan consistently positions AMGEVITA’s differentiation around total value: totality of evidence + supply reliability + device + services + manufacturer reputation.
- Pricing guidance: net price within Tier 1–2 competitor band; differentiate on value rather than undercutting the lowest price.

2) Suggested optimal channels by persona (aligned to traits/preferences)

Table: Personas with traits and optimal channels

| Persona | Traits and preferences | Optimal channels | Content emphasis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Value Payer | Balances quality, cost, and uptake; values non-price factors (reputation, data, supply, services) | - Direct: Account manager and procurement committee meetings - Evidence assets: Value dossiers, white papers, HE models (BIM/CMA), RWE briefs - Digital: Secure micro-portal with clinical/data packs, case studies, RWE updates - Services: Pull-through program briefings | Total value story: supply reliability, robust data (H2H, safety, transition), device/formulation, service model; predictable budget savings through rapid uptake |
| Budget Payer | Cost minimization; price-centric processes (binary tenders, high control) | - Tools: Interactive cost–benefit calculators that quantify risks of lowest-price-only choice and value of reliability/services - Workshops: Educational sessions on multi-criteria evaluation and tender design - Negotiation: In-person/virtual contracting sessions framing multi-criteria scoring | Show that “lowest price ≠ greatest savings” when uptake/continuity risks are considered; highlight adoption enablers (supply, services) that de-risk savings |
| Risk-Averse (payer/HCP-influenced) | Preference for reference brand; safety/efficacy concerns; strong originator ties | - 1:1 engagements: Medical/account-led meetings to address clinical concerns - Scientific education: Transition data, long-term safety, analytical similarity overviews - Expert forums: Webinars/roundtables with KOLs; interactive Q&A - Co-engagement: Joint sessions with trusted physicians/pharmacists | Evidence precedes practice: emphasize totality of evidence, transition data in RA/PsO, post-launch RWE, and Amgen’s manufacturing pedigree |
| Global Market Expansion (strategic audience segment across regions) | Prioritizes regional scaling across rheum, derm, GI via partnerships | - Reports: Regional market insight briefs; success-story casebooks - Partnerships: Collaborations with local providers, societies, procurement bodies - Digital: Targeted campaigns (regional portals, paid media) | Regional proof points, partnership models, and scalability of services and supply reliability to enable rapid, compliant market entry |

Optional additional key decision-maker personas (to accelerate uptake aligned with CSFs 4 and 6)

| Persona | Traits and preferences | Optimal channels | Content emphasis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Prescribing HCPs | Prioritize body of evidence; consider supply, device, services as tie-breakers | - MSL/medical education; congress symposia; peer-reviewed publications - Webinars/CMEs; concise evidence decks; in-clinic device demos - RWE digests; patient support program overviews | Comprehensive totality of evidence; virtually painless citrate-free formulation; SureClick device track record; services that support initiation/adherence |
| Pharmacists | Operational reliability; substitution rules; workflow practicality | - Pharmacy in-services; substitution policy briefings; supply service SLAs - Quick guides; product handling and device training; hotline access | Reliable supply chain; dispensing readiness; how-to on substitution/permission where required; coordination with prescribers |

Reasoning

- Extracted the six CSFs verbatim from the plan summary, then mapped each to the detailed execution activities and governance described across the “Execution Activities,” “How to Win,” and “Organization” pages to formulate succinct SIs per CSF.
- Compiled KPIs where explicitly listed per CSF (pages covering CSF 1, 3, 4, 6, and the consolidated KPI table including CSF 2 and 5) and aligned them to the corresponding CSF row.
- For channels by persona: used the provided NEXT Insight persona breakdowns (Value, Budget, Risk-Averse, and Global Market Expansion) and aligned channels to each persona’s stated traits. Where helpful for uptake (CSFs 4 and 6), added optional rows for Prescribing HCPs and Pharmacists, grounded in brand plan evidence on decision drivers and desired beliefs.
- Kept tables concise, using the brand plan’s value drivers and evidence hierarchy (e.g., “evidence precedes practice,” supply reliability) to prioritize channel types and content focus.

Rationale

- Framework: Strategy execution logic pairs each CSF with enabling SIs and measurable KPIs. This is consistent with the brand plan’s structure (“How to Win” CSFs, “Execution Activities,” “KPIs”).
- Evidence alignment: The channel recommendations mirror the plan’s documented decision drivers by stakeholder: payers (price first, but Value segment considers supply, services, data, device), HCPs (clinical/RWE highest, supply/device/services as tie-breakers), and pharmacists (substitution and operational readiness). This ensures channels deliver the information format each audience trusts and uses.
- Risk/benefit logic for Budget payers: The plan stresses that “lowest price ≠ greatest savings” if adoption fails; hence tools and workshops that quantify uptake risk and value-based tendering are prioritized.
- Differentiation emphasis: For Value payers and HCPs, channels that foreground totality of evidence, supply reliability, device/formulation, and services match CSF 3 and 4, and support CSF 5 (tender shaping) and CSF 6 (pull-through).
- Limitations: The source materials provide historical KPI timelines (2017–2018) and not current-year targets; we report them faithfully and treat them as templates. Market-by-country nuances in tender legality and substitution are acknowledged but not detailed here; channels should be localized accordingly.

References

- Six CSFs overview and definitions; strategic imperatives and focus: “We must have laser focus on 6 Critical Success Factors (CSFs) for AMGEVITA’s launch,” Page 57; Vision and imperatives summaries, Pages 40, 56.
- CSF 1 (Biosimilars Commitment) desired state and KPIs: Page 58; Execution activities and organizational resourcing: Page 83.
- CSF 2 (Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships) KPIs and hiring milestones: Consolidated KPI table, Page 82; Execution activities, Page 83.
- CSF 3 (Elevate Non-Economic Factors) desired state and KPIs: CSF 3 slide, value driver weights, and KPIs, Pages 54, CSF 3 page (no number shown), and “To support… pre-launch engagement,” CSF 3 page.
- CSF 4 (Invest and Promote to Differentiate) story flow, positioning, benefit ladder, and KPIs: Pages 67–70; KPI bullets on Page 70.
- CSF 5 (Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts) value story, pricing band guidance, and KPI: Pages 72–73; KPI consolidated on Page 82.
- CSF 6 (Drive Rapid Uptake) desired state and KPIs: Page 77.
- Consolidated KPI table across CSFs: Page 82.
- Payer segmentation and traits (Budget, Value, Risk-Averse): Pages 24, 52, 71; value driver weights and non-price criteria examples: Page 54 and CSF 3 slide.
- Decision drivers for HCPs (evidence first; supply/device/services as tie-breakers): Page 54; HCP elevator pitch and rationale: Page 69.
- NEXT Insight: Persona channel recommendations for Value Payer, Budget, Risk-Averse, and Global Market Expansion (Generated 10 Oct 2025).
</details>

value multi-criteria when allowed; need operational assurances. | - Formal P&T/tender presentations; technical Q&A. - Procurement portals; site visits/manufacturing quality briefings. - SLA negotiations; service demonstrations. | - Tender criteria exemplars; service catalogs; track-and-trace supply metrics; onboarding/implementation plans. |\n| Prescribing HCPs (Rheum/GI/Derm) | Data-first; then supply, device, services as tie-breakers; need assurance of no compromise vs. Humira. | - MSL scientific exchange; congress symposia/CME. - Peer-reviewed publications; RWE updates. - HCP microsite; device demos; peer-to-peer programs. | - “Totality of evidence” deck (H2H trials, safety extension, transition data) (pp.54, 69). - Device training; citrate-free “virtually painless” message; patient support overviews. |\n| Dispensing Pharmacists | Focus on substitution readiness; need operational clarity and HCP dialogue support. | - Pharmacy in-services; e-learning; quick-reference guides. - Hotline/hub; integration into ordering systems. | - Substitution SOPs; formulary updates; counseling scripts; logistics FAQs. |\n| Patients | Concerned about injection pain, device ease, continuity, support access. | - Patient starter kits; nurse educator outreach. - Injection training videos; SMS/app reminders. - Patient website/portal; hotline. | - Citrate-free “virtually painless” messaging; SureClick device guidance; access/support program details. |\n\nNotes\n- The channels above align with: payer/HCP preferences (EU biosimilar context), AMGEVITA’s brand assets (brand book, digital assets, micro-sites, starter kits), and services/pull-through infrastructure.\n- NEXT Insight persona guidance supports the payer segment channel choices (Value, Budget, Risk-Averse).\n\nActionable insights\n- Prioritize Value accounts for pre-launch tender shaping and multi-criteria contracting; equip AMs with value dossiers, HE models, and RWE.\n- For Budget accounts, lead with HE tools and implementation support that connect price to realized savings via rapid uptake and retention.\n- For Risk-Averse accounts, sequence KOL-led safety/transition evidence and pilot programs to move them toward Value criteria weighting by the time of selection/tender.\n- Stand up dedicated portals/micro-sites for payers and HCPs to centralize evidence, services, and procurement documentation; measure quarterly via CSF 4 KPIs.\n- Ensure pull-through team readiness and pharmacy operations training by launch to capture new starts and drive early share (CSF 6).\n\nReasoning\n- Identified the six CSFs explicitly listed in the brand plan (launch foundation, differentiation, tender readiness, uptake) and pulled the official KPIs from the consolidated KPI list (p.82) and the individual CSF slides (e.g., CSF 4 p.70; CSF 6 p.77; CSF 5 p.74; CSF 3 slide). \n- Mapped SIs from the Execution Activities tables (BBU/Cross-Functional and Value Access & Policy; Commercial: Marketing/Pull-through) and from each CSF’s “Desired State/What Good Looks Like” sections, consolidating overlapping activities (e.g., hiring, tender capability, RWE generation, service build-out) into representative SIs per CSF.\n- For personas and channels, combined: (a) the payer segmentation framework (Value, Budget, Risk-Averse) and their decision weights; (b) HCP value drivers (data first; device/supply/services as tie-breakers); (c) EU engagement channel norms for payers/HCPs from the NEXT insight; and (d) AMGEVITA’s deliverables (brand book, micro-sites, starter kits, patient services) to ensure channel–asset fit. \n- Structured both tables to ensure traceability from strategy (CSFs) → execution (SIs) → measurement (KPIs), and from traits → channels → assets/messages for each persona.\n\nRationale\n- The CSF–SI–KPI triangulation follows standard launch excellence and brand planning logic: define critical outcomes (CSFs), the enabling programs (SIs), and the success metrics (KPIs). The selections here are directly supported by the plan’s CSF slides and execution activity tables. \n- Persona channel recommendations are grounded in the payer segmentation and value-driver evidence in the plan: Value payers consider non-price elements, necessitating content-rich direct engagement (value dossiers, HE models, RWE); Budget payers need price/HE clarity and implementation support; Risk-Averse payers respond to assurance via clinical rigor and KOL endorsements. For HCPs, evidence-first channels (publications, MSL exchange) align with the documented drivers; for pharmacists and patients, operational readiness and support services map to CSF 6 and the services build-out under CSF 4.\n- Limitations/uncertainty: Some context excerpts are partial (e.g., persona table truncation), and several timelines reflect 2017–2018 planning assumptions. Country-specific legal and tender rules vary; channel deployment should be adapted locally. Where explicit persona-channel details were incomplete, we relied on the plan’s stated value drivers and execution assets to propose consistent, evidence-aligned channels.\n\nReferences\n- AMGEVITA Global Brand Plan: Six CSFs overview and narrative (Page 57).\n- KPIs by CSF consolidated table (Page 82).\n- CSF 1: Biosimilars Commitment (Page 58); Execution BBU/Cross-Functional (Page 83).\n- CSF 2: Inflammation Infrastructure & Relationships – hiring/engagement KPIs (Page 82); Execution BBU/Cross-Functional (Page 83).\n- CSF 3: Elevate Non-Economic Decision Factors – desired state and KPIs (CSF 3 slide); Value Access & Policy execution (Page 85); Payer value drivers and weighting (How To Win: CSF 3 slide).\n- CSF 4: Invest and Promote to Differentiate – KPIs (Page 70); HCP value drivers (Page 54); Benefit Ladder (Page 68); Key Story Flow/Elevator Pitch (Page 69); Brand positioning (Page 67).\n- CSF 5: Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts – desired state and KPI (Page 74); Pricing strategy band (Page 73); AMGEVITA Value Story (Page 72); Segmentation/priority accounts (Page 71).\n- CSF 6: Drive Rapid Uptake – desired state and KPIs (Page 77); Execution Marketing: Pull-through team activities (Execution table).\n- Payer Segmentation and proportions (Pages 24, 52, 71).\n- Source of Business and communication guardrails (Pages 54–55).\n- Global deliverables and execution activities (Commercial/Marketing; Value Access & Policy).\n- NEXT Insight Report excerpts: Persona–channel guidance (Value Payer, Budget, Risk-Averse) and preferred EU channels for payers/HCPs; Tabular summaries included in context (no page numbers provided).",

stakeholders: consistently meeting their high standards so they can feel assured that they are doing what’s best for their business and patient needs.<br>- AMGEVITA is backed by a totality of rigorous clinical and analytical evidence, including one of the most comprehensive data sets.<br>- AMGEVITA is administered using the SureClick® Autoinjector, a device patients have been using for over 10 years.<br>- AMGEVITA is formulated citrate-free for virtually painless injections.<br>- Amgen is supporting AMGEVITA with extensive patient and physician resources. |\n\n---\n\n**Source:** AMGEVITA                         "content": "---\n**Page 71**\n\n# How To Win: CSF 5\n\n## Segmentation and identification of priority accounts is a critical early step to pre-launch engagement\n\n---\n\n| Biosimilar ADOPTION | Biosimilar SELECTION | Biosimilar UPTAKE | Biosimilar RETENTION |\n| :-----------------: | :------------------: | :---------------: | :------------------: |\n\n---\n\n### Decision 1: Put biosimilar(s) on formulary?\n\n#### Will the Customer Use Biosimilars?\n\n- **No** → **RISK Averse**\n    - These payers do not control physician choice and their physicians have clinical concern using biosimilars\n    - Have strong relationship with RP manufacturer\n\n    > Over time, it is expected that many of these payers will start using biosimilars and convert to Value Segment customers\n\n- **Yes** → **Is Product Cost the Only Factor Considered?**\n\n    - **No** → **VALUE Segment**\n        - Have procurement processes that include negotiated contracts or multi-source tenders that consider price as well as other decision factors such as the manufacturer, product data and quality, supply reliability, portfolio, services, or partnership\n\n    - **Yes** → **BUDGET Segment**\n        - Most likely to convert to a biosimilar and have procurement processes that are intended to drive rapid price erosion with high control and no/low consideration for other decision factors such as the manufacturer, product data and quality, supply reliability, portfolio, services, or partnership\n\n---\n\n### Decision 2: Which biosimilar(s) to put on formulary?\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\n- **Subject**: Flowchart diagram showing customer segmentation for biosimilar adoption.\n- **Main Elements**: Stepwise flow from initial adoption to retention with color-coded segments for RISK Averse (purple), VALUE (blue), and BUDGET (orange) segments.\n- **Text overlays**: Segment descriptions and procurement behavior criteria.\n- **Visuals**: Green question boxes denote decision points;                         "content": "```markdown\n# Key SWOCs: AMGEVITA is well positioned for success but has to address a few important weaknesses / challenges\n\n---\n\n## ![Strengths Icon] Strengths\n\n- **Data:** One of the most comprehensive clinical data sets; ADA biosimilar with the most published data  \n- **Formulation:** citrate-free / painless  \n- **Proven device:** (>1 million clicks)  \n- **First to settle with Abbvie** provides less uncertainty vs competitors  \n- **Manufacturing & supply reliability/ capabilities**  \n- **Amgen heritage / brand in biologics**  \n- **Learnings defending GCSF** from biosimilar competition  \n- [US/CA]: Legacy and experience in **Rheum and Derm**  \n\n---\n\n## ![Opportunities Icon] Opportunities\n\n- **Successfully differentiate** on unique existing strengths in supply reliability, clinical data, and product attributes\n- **Gain RWE** ahead of competitors and in time for launch\n- Build **differentiated support services**\n- **Portfolio contracts with ONC assets** (& with Enbrel in Canada)\n- **Pre-launch stakeholder engagement** and shaping of tender/ contract criteria (within legal/compliance guardrails)\n- **Be the first** ADA biosimilar to launch where possible; in other markets, accelerate regulatory approval timeline and operational launch readiness\n- Position Amgen as **long-term BioS/biologic partner**\n- **Invest in differentiated capabilities** at the Amgen/ portfolio level (e.g., services, Pull-Through teams)\n- Select Markets: Capitalize on **launch experience with ABP 980**\n\n---\n\n## ![Weaknesses Icon] Weaknesses\n\n- **No data in IBD** (along with all competitors bar BI)\n- **Inflammation presence in EU/IC:** None historically; no GI experience globally\n- **Limited market experience with biosimilars / lack of existing biosimilar portfolio**, versus Pfizer, MSD/Biogen, and Sandoz\n- Traditional organization **focus on innovator products**\n\n---\n\n## ![Challenges Icon] Challenges\n\n- **Reference product defense strategy;** need to assure physicians that AMGEVITA does not require compromises in patient care and customer experience versus Humira\n- **Launching multiple biosimilars** across two TAs (Inflammation and Oncology) over a short period of time\n- **Hyper-competitive, price-sensitive** market with potential to ‘race to the bottom’ on price\n- Market may view **biosimilars as undifferentiated** and/or not view Amgen as a value player\n- **Select markets:** No Amgen presence/ local capability\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\nLower right corner: AMGEVITA® (adalimumab) logo. \nA blue and yellow stylized arc and circle graphic accompanies the brand name.\n[/FIG]\n\n---\n\n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*  \n*Page 43*\n```\n",
