                        "content": "```markdown\nHow To Win: CSF 5\n\n# The AMGEVITA Value Story demonstrates how AMGEVITA and Amgen can help payers achieve desired predictable budget savings, tailored to account-specific needs\n\n---\n\n## Set-Up:\n\n### Establish the Opportunity\nConfirm the account need, and then emphasize conditional benefits.\n\n---\n\n## Problem:\n\n### Highlight Risks of a Sub-Optimal Approach to Biosimilars\nCommunicate risks of choosing any biosimilar.\n\n---\n\n## Solution:\n\n### Promote Advantages of ABP 501\nDemonstrate how ABP 501 addresses risks of not realizing budget savings.\n\n---\n\n## Solution:\n\n### Promote Advantages of Amgen\nDemonstrate how AMGEN addresses risks of not realizing budget savings.\n\n---\n\n### 1\nBudget savings associated with biosimilar adoption provide additional resources necessary to fund innovative treatments that can improve patient care.\n\nA high-quality Humira® biosimilar with clinically rigorous evidence provides significant opportunities for budget savings¹, if there is successful adoption by physicians, pharmacists, and acceptance by patients.\n\n---\n\n### 2\nChoosing a high-quality biosimilar from an experienced and reliable manufacturer is important to maximize value through rapid and successful adoption.\n\n**[Budget]** The least expensive product may not always produce the greatest cost savings².  \nChoosing the product and manufacturer that maximizes opportunity for rapid and successful adoption is important to deliver budget savings.\n\nChoosing the best biosimilar partner on day 1 is important, since no comparative data between biosimilars exists. A poor initial experience can limit budget savings in future contract cycles.\n\n---\n\n### 3\nABP 501 is the Humira® Biosimilar that ensures confidence for rapid and successful adoption to ensure budget savings.\n\nABP 501 has a totality of evidence and extrapolation to all indications based on an analytical, nonclinical, pharmacokinetic and clinical studies.\n\n---\n\n### 4\nAMGEN has applied nearly four decades of experience in developing and manufacturing biologics to its Biosimilar products giving confidence for successful adoption and long-term budget savings.\n\nAMGEN ensures high quality manufacturing standards, uninterrupted product supply, and commercial support.\n\n---\n\n## Result\n\n### Risk Averse\n> **Choose ABP 501 from Amgen as your best Humira® biosimilar choice (according to [insert KOL name(s) & statement]) to ensure physician, pharmacist, and patient confidence for rapid and successful adoption.**\n\n---\n\n### Value\n> **Choose ABP 501 from Amgen as your Humira® Biosimilar offering clinically rigorous evidence, quality manufacturing, and commercial support to achieve predictable budget savings through rapid and successful market adoption.**\n\n---\n\n### Budget\n> **Choose ABP 501 from AMGEN as your Humira® biosimilar offering clinically rigorous evidence, quality manufacturing, and commercial support to achieve the greatest budget savings.**\n\n---\n\n¹As demonstrated by a BIM.  \n²As demonstrated by a HEOR Tendering Tool.\n\nAmgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\n- **Bottom right corner:** AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo with blue and yellow curved lines.\n[/FIG]\n\n---\n\n**Sidebar (Top-Right Boxes):**\n- **VISION & GOALS**\n- **WHERE TO PLAY?**\n- **HOW TO WIN?**\n- **ORGANIZATION**\n\n---\n\n**Page Number:** 72\n```\n",

                        "id": 152682,
                        "content": "```markdown\nPayers can be categorized into 3 segments: Value, Risk, & Budget. Value accounts are most receptive to Amgen’s value proposition\n\n---\n\n| Biosimilar ADOPTION | → | Biosimilar SELECTION | → | Biosimilar UPTAKE | → | Biosimilar RETENTION |\n|:-------------------:|---|:-------------------:|---|:-----------------:|---|:-------------------:|\n\n---\n\n### BUDGET  \n*\"Cost minimization\"*\n- No or low consideration for decision factors other than price\n- Procurement processes drive rapid price erosion (e.g., binary tenders, price-blind contracting)\n- High control versus physicians\n\n---\n\n### VALUE  \n*\"Balance Quality, Cost & Uptake\"*  \n- **Achieve budget savings by selecting a high-quality product at a good value**\n- **Negotiate contracts / multi-source tenders considering overall value of offering**  \n  *(e.g. manufacturer, product data and quality, supply reliability, portfolio (US/CA), services, and partnership)*\n\n---\n\n### RISK-AVERSE  \n*\"Physician Choice +/- Contractual Relationship\"*  \n- Initially, no or limited conversion to biosimilars – intend to stay with branded product; but expect some biosimilar adoption over the longer run\n- Low control versus physicians *(physicians have a high degree of clinical concern with biosimilars as a class, and/or have strong relationships with Abbvie)*\n- **Early engagement critical as these payers are expected to convert to value over time**  \n  *(ensure selection of AMGEVITA when biosimilar selection occurs)*\n\n---\n\n> [FIG]\n> Amgen AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo in bottom right  \n> Blue and gold color scheme\n> Three colored blocks representing segments (orange for Budget, blue for Value, purple for Risk-Averse)\n> A process arrow at the top showing 4 biosimilar commercial phases: Adoption → Selection → Uptake → Retention\n> [/FIG]\n\n---\n\n**Next Step for Countries:** Identify accounts and size segments\n\n---\n\n*Source: Payer Segmentation Research*  \n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*  \n\n*Page 24*\n```",

                        "id": 152683,
                        "content": "```markdown\n# Key Insights and Implications for AMGEVITA Strategy\n\n| Insights | Implications for Strategy |\n|----------|--------------------------|\n| **Market Opp’nity** |  |\n| • Crowded market with many options for HCPs, achieving share of voice will be challenging <br> • Primary competition is RP and other ADA BioS, who will compete for share gain within existing pool of ADA PTs | • Hypercompetitive market combined with rapid timeline to launch necessitates being focused: launch focus should be on share gain vs Humira & other ADA BioS <br> • Early targeting and engagement of key accounts |\n| **Key Decision Points** |  |\n| • Most markets are expected to see the RP plus one BioS on formulary, where the payer exercises soft or medium controls for biosimilar uptake, leaving at least some prescription choice to the HCP | • In Soft/ Medium payer control markets:<br> • To get on formulary, AMGEVITA will primarily compete with other biosimilars <br> • To get prescribed once on formulary, AMGEVITA will typically compete with RP but NOT other BioS |\n| **BioS Adoption** |  |\n| • 3 Payer segments: Value, Risk Averse, & Budget. Value is most receptive to Amgen | • Identify & archetype accounts, map decision-makers <br> • Prioritize and engage value accounts |\n| **BioS Selection** |  |\n| • Price is #1 determinant of biosimilar selection <br> • Value payers will include other criteria | • Elevate the importance of non-economic tender/ contract criteria |\n| |  |\n| • Sandoz, Pfizer, and Biogen/MSD have an advantage over Amgen in terms of (Ex-US/CA) inflammation presence, biosimilars experience, and portfolio <br> • However, Amgen has strengths in supply reliability, clinical data, and product attributes | • Educate key decision makers on strengths in supply reliability, clinical data, and product attributes <br> • Invest in further differentiation via best-in-class services, RWE, portfolio/innovative contracting <br> • Price competitively |\n| **BioS Uptake** |  |\n| • Stakeholders target BioS for new starts, do not expect to switch stable PTs in initial years (except select mkts) <br> • Prescribers value data above all else; and will also consider device, supply & services | • Prioritize new patient starts for proactive uptake <br> • Excellence in body of evidence (clinical data, RWE), supply, device, & services can support rapid uptake. |\n| **BioS Retention** |  |\n| • At contract renewals, late-entrants can displace incumbents via discounts; several late entrants are Tier 2/3 and will place downward price pressure <br> • Majority of HCPs & Phams expect to feel comfortable switching between biosimilars | • Be first in the market to have a critical mass of contracts with pre-launch engagement and education <br> • Earn following years’ contract with this year's performance; and build retention with services, RWE <br> • Need a nimble organization to enable rapid decisions |\n\n---\n\n*Page 40*\n\n*Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute*\n```\n[No images to describe on this page.]\n",

                        "content": "```markdown\n# Biosimilars strategy – executive summary\n\n---\n\n## A Compelling Market Opportunity …\n\n- Despite a history of over 10 years, the BioS market is still in its inception as the majority of launched biosimilars are GCSFs and ESAs and only a small number of mAbs have been launched to date (1 in the US, 4 in EU)\n- However, over the next 3 years, the biosimilars market will pass a critical inflection point with over $50B worth of oncology and inflammation mAbs losing exclusivity through 2020\n\n---\n\n## … Integral to Amgen’s Corporate Strategy\n\n- Amgen currently has 10 biosimilars in development which are forecast to contribute significantly to Amgen’s corporate topline by 2025, accounting for 25% of corporate growth between 2016–2025\n- In addition to driving growth, biosimilars will serve as a catalyst for innovation (e.g. by innovating stakeholder engagement through VBHC), and help strengthen Amgen’s position and brand in core therapeutic areas\n\n---\n\n## Multi-Dimensional Dynamics …\n\n- The competitive landscape is rapidly changing along a multi-dimensional set of reference product, biosimilars and NME competitors, and will lead to significant shifts in the future market landscape\n- In parallel, structural differences between innovator and biosimilars business and an evolving customer landscape position payers as primary decision makers, focused on value creation through contracting and emergence of VBHC deals; this creates unique requirements for our biosimilars business model and proactive management of critical SWOTs\n\n---\n\n## … Shape New Success Requirements\n\n- At the outset, Amgen’s biosimilars strategy was built around differentiation via Amgen’s biologics expertise and brand\n- Given the changing marketplace, success will require additional focus along 3 strategic imperatives:\n    1. **Shape biosimilars market** and set a high bar for biosimilars\n    2. **Be (among) first to launch** with critical mass and ensure rapid penetration\n    3. **Differentiate from competitors** (biosimilars and RP*) via **total value of Amgen solutions** **\n\n---\n\n\\* RP = Reference Product  \n\\** This encompasses (i) **multi-prong differentiation of Amgen Biosimilars** via product differentiation / LCM, services, Amgen portfolio contracting and VBHC solutions, and (ii) **proactive portfolio management**, integrated across innovator and biosimilars business to strengthen Amgen portfolio contracting capability and help to adjust to changing competitive landscape\n\n---\n\n> Amgen Confidential – Do Not Distribute\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\n- Bottom right: AMGEVITA (adalimumab) logo\n[/FIG]\n\n**Page Number**: 08 (visible bottom right)\n```\n",

While specific data on preferred channels for Amgevita is limited, general trends and strategies can be outlined based on the broader context of biosimilar adoption in Europe.\n\n### Payers' Strategies\n\nPayers in the EU often employ several strategies to manage biosimilar adoption:\n\n1. **Formulary Management:** Payers may give preferential status to biosimilars over originators or cover both at parity, depending on cost savings and clinical equivalence[4].\n2. **Rebate Negotiations:** Payers negotiate rebates with manufacturers, which can influence the adoption of biosimilars versus originators[4].\n3. **Educational Initiatives:** Some payers support educational programs to increase awareness and acceptance of biosimilars among HCPs and patients[8].\n\n### Healthcare Professionals' (HCPs) Engagement\n\nHCPs engage with biosimilars through:\n\n1. **Clinical Evidence:** HCPs rely on clinical trials and real-world evidence to assess biosimilarity and safety[10][16].\n2. **Professional Guidelines:** Many HCPs follow guidelines from professional societies that endorse biosimilars as effective alternatives[10].\n3. **Patient Education:** HCPs often educate patients about the benefits and risks of biosimilars, which can influence treatment choices[8].\n\n---\n\n### Table: Preferred Channels for Biosimilar Engagement in EU Markets (Amgevita <details><summary>Click to OLD Answer</summary>
Main Answer

1) Summary of CSFs, SIs, and KPIs from the AMGEVITA brand plan

Table: CSFs with aligned Strategic Initiatives (SIs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)

| CSF | What it means | Core Strategic Initiatives (SIs) | Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) |
|---|---|---|---|
| CSF 1: Biosimilars Commitment | Commit enterprise resources, governance, and pace suitable for a biosimilar business | - Country-level business cases and forecasts; budget allocation - Establish nimble contracting/pricing governance and DAI - Align commercial incentives to biosimilar vision - Train internal teams on the “Amgen biosimilars story” - Prioritize launch sequences and resource biosimilars/inflammation at global, regional, country levels | - By Dec 2018: Country forecast complete - By Dec/Jan 2018: Resource assessment complete; budget allocated - By Apr 1, 2018: Contracting and pricing governance established |
| CSF 2: Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships | Rapidly build TA infrastructure (rheumatology, GI prioritized) and external presence | - Hire marketing, VAP, medical, RMLs, field force - Transfer learnings from US/CA; champion rotations - Identify rheum/GI OLs and procurement committee members; schedule meetings | - By Jan 1, 2018: Marketing, VAP, Medical team hired - By Apr 1, 2018: RMLs hired; OLs and procurement members identified - By Jul 1, 2018: Field force hired; meetings with >80% OLs/procurement |
| CSF 3: Elevate Importance of Non-Economic Decision Factors | Increase weight of supply, data, product, services, manufacturer reputation in selection | - Monthly pre-launch engagement plan with decision-makers - Country-level payer communications (white papers) - Map decision journeys; segment accounts; HEOR tools (BIM, CMA, Account calculators) - Develop tender capability; define non-price criteria and weights | - By Apr 1, 2018: >80% of top priority accounts engaged - By Jul 1, 2018: 100% top priority + >50% second priority engaged - Quarterly: % of top accounts increasing weight of non-price criteria - By Launch: 100% priority accounts place country-defined X% weight on non-price criteria |
| CSF 4: Invest and Promote to Differentiate AMGEVITA | Build on strengths (supply, data, device) and invest in services and RWE to be #1 ADA | - Brand book, global launch campaign, localized assets - Country micro-sites; communication platform - Build patient/HCP services; hire hub/service teams - Collect, publish, and communicate early-country RWE - HCP “elevator pitch” focused on totality of evidence, supply, device, services, reputation - Develop starter kits; demo kits | - Quarterly (from Apr 2018): % top payers/committees who consider AMGEVITA #1 ADA at selection (price parity assumed) - Quarterly (from Apr 2018): % top prescribers who consider AMGEVITA #1 at prescription decision |
| CSF 5: Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts at Launch | Engage pre-launch to shape criteria and secure contracts at launch (within legal/compliance) | - Map tender/contracting timelines and requirements - Pre-launch tender/contract framework discussions (as permitted) - Establish portfolio/innovative contracting strategy and governance - Global/region/country pricing policies; price in Tier 1–2 band (avoid race-to-bottom) | - By Launch: Leading share of contracts/tenders won among priority accounts versus ADA biosimilar competitors |
| CSF 6: Drive Rapid AMGEVITA Uptake | Establish pull-through engine and cross-functional coordination to convert access into Rx | - Build biosimilar Pull-Through Team; define account-specific pull-through - Prepare hub support; V&A contacts; sales force readiness - Develop tools (BIM, training), demo and starter kits - Coordinate targets and resources across functions | - Monthly: % of new ADA starts on AMGEVITA (vs. LRP) - Monthly: % of existing Humira patients placed on AMGEVITA (vs. LRP) - Sources: HCP survey, IMS |

Notes
- The plan consistently positions AMGEVITA’s differentiation around total value: totality of evidence + supply reliability + device + services + manufacturer reputation.
- Pricing guidance: net price within Tier 1–2 competitor band; differentiate on value rather than undercutting the lowest price.

2) Suggested optimal channels by persona (aligned to traits/preferences)

Table: Personas with traits and optimal channels

| Persona | Traits and preferences | Optimal channels | Content emphasis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Value Payer | Balances quality, cost, and uptake; values non-price factors (reputation, data, supply, services) | - Direct: Account manager and procurement committee meetings - Evidence assets: Value dossiers, white papers, HE models (BIM/CMA), RWE briefs - Digital: Secure micro-portal with clinical/data packs, case studies, RWE updates - Services: Pull-through program briefings | Total value story: supply reliability, robust data (H2H, safety, transition), device/formulation, service model; predictable budget savings through rapid uptake |
| Budget Payer | Cost minimization; price-centric processes (binary tenders, high control) | - Tools: Interactive cost–benefit calculators that quantify risks of lowest-price-only choice and value of reliability/services - Workshops: Educational sessions on multi-criteria evaluation and tender design - Negotiation: In-person/virtual contracting sessions framing multi-criteria scoring | Show that “lowest price ≠ greatest savings” when uptake/continuity risks are considered; highlight adoption enablers (supply, services) that de-risk savings |
| Risk-Averse (payer/HCP-influenced) | Preference for reference brand; safety/efficacy concerns; strong originator ties | - 1:1 engagements: Medical/account-led meetings to address clinical concerns - Scientific education: Transition data, long-term safety, analytical similarity overviews - Expert forums: Webinars/roundtables with KOLs; interactive Q&A - Co-engagement: Joint sessions with trusted physicians/pharmacists | Evidence precedes practice: emphasize totality of evidence, transition data in RA/PsO, post-launch RWE, and Amgen’s manufacturing pedigree |
| Global Market Expansion (strategic audience segment across regions) | Prioritizes regional scaling across rheum, derm, GI via partnerships | - Reports: Regional market insight briefs; success-story casebooks - Partnerships: Collaborations with local providers, societies, procurement bodies - Digital: Targeted campaigns (regional portals, paid media) | Regional proof points, partnership models, and scalability of services and supply reliability to enable rapid, compliant market entry |

Optional additional key decision-maker personas (to accelerate uptake aligned with CSFs 4 and 6)

| Persona | Traits and preferences | Optimal channels | Content emphasis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Prescribing HCPs | Prioritize body of evidence; consider supply, device, services as tie-breakers | - MSL/medical education; congress symposia; peer-reviewed publications - Webinars/CMEs; concise evidence decks; in-clinic device demos - RWE digests; patient support program overviews | Comprehensive totality of evidence; virtually painless citrate-free formulation; SureClick device track record; services that support initiation/adherence |
| Pharmacists | Operational reliability; substitution rules; workflow practicality | - Pharmacy in-services; substitution policy briefings; supply service SLAs - Quick guides; product handling and device training; hotline access | Reliable supply chain; dispensing readiness; how-to on substitution/permission where required; coordination with prescribers |

Reasoning

- Extracted the six CSFs verbatim from the plan summary, then mapped each to the detailed execution activities and governance described across the “Execution Activities,” “How to Win,” and “Organization” pages to formulate succinct SIs per CSF.
- Compiled KPIs where explicitly listed per CSF (pages covering CSF 1, 3, 4, 6, and the consolidated KPI table including CSF 2 and 5) and aligned them to the corresponding CSF row.
- For channels by persona: used the provided NEXT Insight persona breakdowns (Value, Budget, Risk-Averse, and Global Market Expansion) and aligned channels to each persona’s stated traits. Where helpful for uptake (CSFs 4 and 6), added optional rows for Prescribing HCPs and Pharmacists, grounded in brand plan evidence on decision drivers and desired beliefs.
- Kept tables concise, using the brand plan’s value drivers and evidence hierarchy (e.g., “evidence precedes practice,” supply reliability) to prioritize channel types and content focus.

Rationale

- Framework: Strategy execution logic pairs each CSF with enabling SIs and measurable KPIs. This is consistent with the brand plan’s structure (“How to Win” CSFs, “Execution Activities,” “KPIs”).
- Evidence alignment: The channel recommendations mirror the plan’s documented decision drivers by stakeholder: payers (price first, but Value segment considers supply, services, data, device), HCPs (clinical/RWE highest, supply/device/services as tie-breakers), and pharmacists (substitution and operational readiness). This ensures channels deliver the information format each audience trusts and uses.
- Risk/benefit logic for Budget payers: The plan stresses that “lowest price ≠ greatest savings” if adoption fails; hence tools and workshops that quantify uptake risk and value-based tendering are prioritized.
- Differentiation emphasis: For Value payers and HCPs, channels that foreground totality of evidence, supply reliability, device/formulation, and services match CSF 3 and 4, and support CSF 5 (tender shaping) and CSF 6 (pull-through).
- Limitations: The source materials provide historical KPI timelines (2017–2018) and not current-year targets; we report them faithfully and treat them as templates. Market-by-country nuances in tender legality and substitution are acknowledged but not detailed here; channels should be localized accordingly.

References

- Six CSFs overview and definitions; strategic imperatives and focus: “We must have laser focus on 6 Critical Success Factors (CSFs) for AMGEVITA’s launch,” Page 57; Vision and imperatives summaries, Pages 40, 56.
- CSF 1 (Biosimilars Commitment) desired state and KPIs: Page 58; Execution activities and organizational resourcing: Page 83.
- CSF 2 (Inflammation Infrastructure and Relationships) KPIs and hiring milestones: Consolidated KPI table, Page 82; Execution activities, Page 83.
- CSF 3 (Elevate Non-Economic Factors) desired state and KPIs: CSF 3 slide, value driver weights, and KPIs, Pages 54, CSF 3 page (no number shown), and “To support… pre-launch engagement,” CSF 3 page.
- CSF 4 (Invest and Promote to Differentiate) story flow, positioning, benefit ladder, and KPIs: Pages 67–70; KPI bullets on Page 70.
- CSF 5 (Shape Tenders & Ensure Contracts) value story, pricing band guidance, and KPI: Pages 72–73; KPI consolidated on Page 82.
- CSF 6 (Drive Rapid Uptake) desired state and KPIs: Page 77.
- Consolidated KPI table across CSFs: Page 82.
- Payer segmentation and traits (Budget, Value, Risk-Averse): Pages 24, 52, 71; value driver weights and non-price criteria examples: Page 54 and CSF 3 slide.
- Decision drivers for HCPs (evidence first; supply/device/services as tie-breakers): Page 54; HCP elevator pitch and rationale: Page 69.
- NEXT Insight: Persona channel recommendations for Value Payer, Budget, Risk-Averse, and Global Market Expansion (Generated 10 Oct 2025).

initiation checklist (volume status, diuretic adjustment); ensure formulary/PA playbooks are available clinic-side |\n| Nephrology | Late referral limits eligible window (eGFR <20); variable adoption in non-albuminuric CKD; concern about advanced CKD starts and polypharmacy; competing priorities (anemia/bone/mineral, access planning) | Patients present late; uncertainty about benefit in low-albuminuric subsets; safety monitoring overhead | % stage 3\u20134 CKD on SGLT2i; time-to-start after nephro intake; % eligible-but-uninitiated; eGFR slope and UACR change | Partner upstream to pull-forward referrals (stage 3b, high UACR); standing order sets for SGLT2i assessment at intake; nurse-led start-and-monitor protocols; align with RAAS/finerenone sequencing where indicated |\n\nActionable next steps\n- Make eGFR+UACR universal in T2D/HTN annual panels and close the loop on abnormal UACR within 90 days.\n- Stand up a unified cardiorenal SGLT2i pathway (ownership, thresholds, labs, monitoring) adopted by PCP, cardiology, and nephrology.\n- Track SGLT2i initiation rate and time-to-initiation for eligible CKD patients by specialty; set quarterly improvement targets.\n- Reduce access friction: implement ePA, publish payer-specific PA guides, and monitor abandonment; target <15%.\n- Launch a short \u201cstart smart\u201d protocol: volume status check, diuretic adjustment if needed, sick-day rules, early follow-up at 2\u20134 weeks.\n- Create rapid referral triggers (e.g., UACR \u2265300 mg/g, rapid eGFR decline) and monitor referral timeliness.\n\nReasoning\n1) Parsed the request into two deliverables: a cross-specialty framework of CKD CSFs/SIs/KPIs and specialty-specific initiation gaps. 2) Identified core CKD processes that drive outcomes (screening, guideline-concordant therapy, access, monitoring, coordination) from the context (KDIGO-aligned staging, EMPA-KIDNEY outcomes, and quality frameworks listing eGFR/UACR testing, ACEi/ARB use, control of BP/A1c/LDL). 3) Selected SIs (leading process signals) and KPIs (quantifiable endpoints) that are measurable within typical EHR/claims datasets and used in CKD quality programs. 4) For initiation gaps, mapped barriers and remediation to each specialty\u2019s typical workflow and role: PCP (screening, staging, PA), cardiology (cardiorenal integration, albuminuria), nephrology (late referral, advanced CKD nuances). 5) Grounded benefits and targets in EMPA-KIDNEY (28% RRR progression/CV death; 14% hospitalization reduction) and CKD quality indicator literature (e.g., GFR/albuminuria testing KPIs, BP/A1c/LDL control gaps), noting that numeric targets are directional and should be calibrated to local baselines.\n\nRationale\n- Principles: Use of established quality frameworks (screening, ACEi/ARB optimization, risk-factor control), guideline-aligned therapy initiation (KDIGO), and high-impact outcome evidence (EMPA-KIDNEY) to define CSFs. SIs represent proximal process changes predicting improvement; KPIs are outcome/process measures suitable for dashboards and value-based care contracts. - Specialty tailoring: Initiation barriers differ by role\u2014PCPs face time/PA hurdles; cardiologists prioritize CV endpoints and need albuminuria integration; nephrologists face late referrals and advanced-stage complexity. - Limitations/uncertainty: Exact performance baselines (e.g., current SGLT2i penetration, BP/A1c/LDL goal attainment) vary by system; published percentages cited in the context are from specific studies/populations and should be considered directional. Targets provided are pragmatic stretch goals, not mandates; they should be customized to your local data and payer mix. - Assumptions: CKD program aims to expand SGLT2i use in eligible patients per label/guidelines; formulary access and ePA are achievable; cross-specialty governance can harmonize pathways.\n\nReferences\n- EMPA-KIDNEY trial summary (internal): JAR-INT-CED-FY25-V2.2, Section 14.3 Chronic Kidney Disease (CKD) \u2014 28% RRR in CKD progression/CV death; 14% RRR all-cause hospitalization.\n- Value/HEOR framing for CKD: JAR-INT-HEORVAL-FY25-V1.0 \u2014 Pillar 3: Slowing CKD progression and hospitalization cost offsets.\n- Patient journey/operational insights for CKD starts and monitoring: JAR-INT-PJOURNEY-HF_CKD-FY25-V1.0 \u2014 Adding protective therapy; monitoring; counseling workflows.\n- Guideline context (as referenced in internal materials): KDIGO recommendations to use SGLT2i broadly in CKD with eGFR \u226520 mL/min/1.73 m\u00b2 and/or albuminuria (see KDIGO Diabetes in CKD and CKD guidelines).\n- CKD quality indicators (screening, BP/A1c/LDL targets, anemia/bone disease metrics): Context cites ISAHD CKD KPIs document and a CKD quality study (PMC11531362) demonstrating real-world gaps in BP, HbA1c, and LDL target attainment.\n- Underuse and adoption barriers for SGLT2i in CKD (cross-specialty): NEXT Insight Report excerpts and internal persona/channel strategy documents (JAR-INT-HCP-FY25-V2.0; JAR-INT-SBF-FY25-V2.1).

EMR best-practice alerts for SGLT2i eligibility; one-page start algorithm + “sick day” counseling; ePA automation; define referral triggers (high UACR, rapid eGFR decline) |\n| Cardiology | SGLT2i starts limited to overt HF; CKD risk (albuminuria) not routinely assessed; hesitation to “own” CKD initiation if no HF; diuretic/volume concerns | CV event focus; albuminuria not routinely ordered; workflow lacks CKD prompts; role ambiguity with PCP/nephrology | Cardiology share of SGLT2i starts in CKD; % HF+CKD on SGLT2i; time-to-start post abnormal UACR; all-cause hospitalization | Add UACR to HF/ASCVD lab panels; co-authored cardiorenal pathway clarifying initiation responsibilities; initiation checklist (volume status, diuretic adjustment); ensure formulary/PA playbooks are available clinic-side |\n| Nephrology | Late referral limits eligible window (eGFR <20); variable adoption in non-albuminuric CKD; concern about advanced CKD starts and polypharmacy; competing priorities (anemia/bone/mineral, access planning) | Patients present late; uncertainty about benefit in low-albuminuric subsets; safety monitoring overhead | % stage 3–4 CKD on SGLT2i; time-to-start after nephro intake; % eligible-but-uninitiated; eGFR slope and UACR change | Partner upstream to pull-forward referrals (stage 3b, high UACR); standing order sets for SGLT2i assessment at intake; nurse-led start-and-monitor protocols; align with RAAS/finerenone sequencing where indicated |\n\nActionable next steps\n- Make eGFR+UACR universal in T2D/HTN annual panels and close the loop on abnormal UACR within 90 days.\n- Stand up a unified cardiorenal SGLT2i pathway (ownership, thresholds, labs, monitoring) adopted by PCP, cardiology, and nephrology.\n- Track SGLT2i initiation rate and time-to-initiation for eligible CKD patients by specialty; set quarterly improvement targets.\n- Reduce access friction: implement ePA, publish payer-specific PA guides, and monitor abandonment; target <15%.\n- Launch a short “start smart” protocol: volume status check, diuretic adjustment if needed, sick-day rules, early follow-up at 2–4 weeks.\n- Create rapid referral triggers (e.g., UACR ≥300 mg/g, rapid eGFR decline) and monitor referral timeliness.\n\nReasoning\n1) Parsed the request into two deliverables: a cross-specialty framework of CKD CSFs/SIs/KPIs and specialty-specific initiation gaps. 2) Identified core CKD processes that drive outcomes (screening, guideline-concordant therapy, access, monitoring, coordination) from the context (KDIGO-aligned staging, EMPA-KIDNEY outcomes, and quality frameworks listing eGFR/UACR testing, ACEi/ARB use, control of BP/A1c/LDL). 3) Selected SIs (leading process signals) and KPIs (quantifiable endpoints) that are measurable within typical EHR/claims datasets and used in CKD quality programs. 4) For initiation gaps, mapped barriers and remediation to each specialty’s typical workflow and role: PCP (screening, staging, PA), cardiology (cardiorenal integration, albuminuria), nephrology (late referral, advanced CKD nuances). 5) Grounded benefits and targets in EMPA-KIDNEY (28% RRR progression/CV death; 14% hospitalization reduction) and CKD quality indicator literature (e.g., GFR/albuminuria testing KPIs, BP/A1c/LDL control gaps), noting that numeric targets are directional and should be calibrated to local baselines.\n\nRationale\n- Principles: Use of established quality frameworks (screening, ACEi/ARB optimization, risk-factor control), guideline-aligned therapy initiation (KDIGO), and high-impact outcome evidence (EMPA-KIDNEY) to define CSFs. SIs represent proximal process changes predicting improvement; KPIs are outcome/process measures suitable for dashboards and value-based care contracts. - Specialty tailoring: Initiation barriers differ by role—PCPs face time/PA hurdles; cardiologists prioritize CV endpoints and need albuminuria integration; nephrologists face late referrals and advanced-stage complexity. - Limitations/uncertainty: Exact performance baselines (e.g., current SGLT2i penetration, BP/A1c/LDL goal attainment) vary by system; published percentages cited in the context are from specific studies/populations and should be considered directional. Targets provided are pragmatic stretch goals, not mandates; they should be customized to your local data and payer mix. - Assumptions: CKD program aims to expand SGLT2i use in eligible patients per label/guidelines; formulary access and ePA are achievable; cross-specialty governance can harmonize pathways.\n\nReferences\n- EMPA-KIDNEY trial summary (internal): JAR-INT-CED-FY25-V2.2, Section 14.3 Chronic Kidney Disease (CKD) — 28% RRR in CKD progression/CV death; 14% RRR all-cause hospitalization.\n- Value/HEOR framing for CKD: JAR-INT-HEORVAL-FY25-V1.0 — Pillar 3: Slowing CKD progression and hospitalization cost offsets.\n- Patient journey/operational insights for CKD starts and monitoring: JAR-INT-PJOURNEY-HF_CKD-FY25-V1.0 — Adding protective therapy; monitoring; counseling workflows.\n- Guideline context (as referenced in internal materials): KDIGO recommendations to use SGLT2i broadly in CKD with eGFR ≥20 mL/min/1.73 m² and/or albuminuria (see KDIGO Diabetes in CKD and CKD guidelines).\n- CKD quality indicators (screening, BP/A1c/LDL targets, anemia/bone disease metrics): Context cites ISAHD CKD KPIs document and a CKD quality study (PMC11531362) demonstrating real-world gaps in BP, HbA1c, and LDL target attainment.\n- Underuse and adoption barriers for SGLT2i in CKD (cross-specialty): NEXT Insight Report excerpts and internal persona/channel strategy documents (JAR-INT-HCP-FY25-V2.0; JAR-INT-SBF-FY25-V2.1).",

Key Supporting Points & Evidence:**\n\n  - *What are the main reasons to believe the proposition?* List key data points, clinical evidence, or rationales.\n\n  - MUST reference specific data from approved PI/Clinical Dossier (Ref: Doc 2).\n\n  - **Example:**\n    1. EMPA-KIDNEY showed 28% RRR in CKD progression/CV death (HR 0.72).\n    2. Reduced all-cause hospitalizations by 14% (HR 0.86).\n    3. Benefit shown in patients WITH and WITHOUT T2D.\n    4. Indicated down to eGFR 20 mL/min/1.73 m².\n    5. Once-daily oral dosing.\n\n---\n\n- **G. Desired Audience Response / Call to Action:**\n\n  - *What do we want the audience to THINK, FEEL, and DO after seeing this communication?*\n\n  - Make the \"DO\" specific and actionable.\n\n  - **Example:** THINK: \"Jardiance offers meaningful kidney protection I should consider for my CKD patients.\" FEEL: \"Confident I can help slow progression.\" DO: \"Identify CKD patients meeting criteria (eGFR/UACR) and consider initiating Jardiance 10mg / Visit JardianceHCP.com/CKD for resources.\"\n\n---\n\n- **H. Tone of Voice:**\n\n  - *Describe the desired personality and feeling of the communication.*\n\n  - Reference Brand Voice Guide (Ref: Doc 10) and tailor if needed.\n\n  - **Example:** Confident, Clear, Urgent (Time to Act), Supportive, Scientific yet Accessible (for PCP audience).",

                        "id": 152708,
                        "content": "```markdown\n- Clinical Anchor: EMPEROR Program showed **21-25% RRR in CV Death or HHF** across HFrEF & HFpEF, plus significant reduction (~27-30%) in total (first + recurrent) HF hospitalizations.\n- Economic Angle: High frequency and cost of repeat HF hospitalizations is a major burden for payers. Reducing total HHF events directly translates to significant potential cost savings for the health plan / system. Position Jardiance as an investment to reduce downstream acute care costs.\n- Supporting HEOR Concepts: BIMs focused on HF populations. CEAs vs. standard care components without SGLT2i. Real-World Evidence (RWE) studies (e.g., EMPRISE) demonstrating similar hospitalization reductions in routine practice.\n\n**Pillar 3: Slowing Chronic Kidney Disease Progression & Associated Costs:**\n  - Clinical Anchor: EMPA-KIDNEY showed **28% RRR in CKD progression or CV death**, plus **14% RRR in all-cause hospitalization**.\n  - Economic Angle: Slowing progression delays or avoids extremely high costs associated with End-Stage Kidney Disease (ESKD) requiring dialysis (>$80k/patient/year) or transplantation. Reducing all-cause hospitalizations in this high-risk population also provides significant cost offsets.\n  - Supporting HEOR Concepts: BIMs modeling impact on CKD progression rates and dialysis costs. CEAs demonstrating long-term cost-effectiveness in delaying ESKD. Hospitalization cost-offset analyses based on EMPA-KIDNEY data.\n\n### 4. Key Data Inputs for Models/Dossiers:\n\n- Efficacy data (HRs, ARRs) from EMPA-REG, EMPEROR, EMPA-KIDNEY.\n- Safety/tolerability data from clinical trials.\n- Hospitalization rates and costs (literature-based, claims data).\n- Dialysis costs (USRDS data).\n- Drug acquisition costs (WAC, expected Net Price).\n- Quality of Life data (e.g., KCCQ scores from EMPEROR, utility values from literature) for QALY calculations.\n- RWE data supporting trial findings in real-world populations.\n\n### 5. Communication Guidance:\n\n- Value story must be presented using AMCP format dossier or other payer-appropriate, evidence-based formats.\n- All models and analyses must use transparent, validated methodologies and assumptions.\n- Communications tailored to specific payer/HTA body priorities (e.g., budget impact focus vs. long-term cost-effectiveness).\n- Must be delivered by trained Market Access / HEOR personnel.\n```\n(No tables, equations, or images were present on the page. Purpose:\nThis document summarizes the core Health Economics and Outcomes Research (HEOR) value arguments for Jardiance, intended primarily for internal strategic alignment and to inform communications with US Payers, HTA bodies, and Formulary Committees. This information **is distinct from promotional messaging used with HCPs** and requires adaptation and appropriate evidence dossiers (e.g., AMCP Format Dossier) for external payer engagement by Market Access teams.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Target Audience for Value Story:\nUS Payers (Commercial PBMs, Medicare Part D Plans, Medicaid Directors), Integrated Delivery Networks (IDNs), Hospital Formulary Committees (P&T), Health Technology Assessment (HTA) bodies (where applicable globally).\n\n---\n\n### 3. Core Value Proposition Pillars:\nJardiance delivers significant clinical value across T2D, HF, and CKD by reducing major morbidity and mortality events, which translates into potential economic value for healthcare systems through cost offsets.\n\n- **Pillar 1: Reducing Costly Cardiovascular Events (T2D + Established CVD):**\n    - **Clinical Anchor:** EMPA-REG OUTCOME demonstrated **38% RRR in CV Death and 35% RRR in HHF**.\n    - **Economic Angle:** Reduction in CV death avoids substantial end-of-life costs. Reduction in HF hospitalizations avoids high-cost acute care episodes (avg. HF hospitalization cost ~ 15k–20k). Frame as potential cost offset or budget impact neutral/favorable over medium term for high-risk T2D populations.\n    - **Supporting HEOR Concepts:** Budget Impact Models (BIMs) projecting plan costs with/without increased Jardiance utilization. Cost-effectiveness analyses (CEAs) vs older therapies (e.g., SU, DPP4i) often showing favorable ICER (Incremental Cost-Effectiveness Ratio) below accepted willingness-to-pay thresholds (e.g., <$100k/QALY gained) based on published models.\n\n- **Pillar 2: Reducing the Burden of Heart Failure Hospitalizations (Across EF Spectrum):**\n\n---\n```",

Can be perceived barrier, particularly for PCPs.\n- Ongoing payer pressure impacting net price (GtN **-53%** US average) and requiring access hurdles (PA/ST).\n- Modest weight loss effect compared to GLP-1 RAs.\n- Messaging complexity across three major, distinct indications.\n\n---\n\n### • Opportunities:\n- Capitalize on large, undertreated CKD population – significant growth driver.\n- Drive earlier adoption in HF pathway (per guidelines) – capture incident share.\n- Reinforce cardiorenal value proposition in T2D segment beyond glucose control.\n- Leverage real-world evidence (RWE) generation (e.g., EMPERISE study) to support value proposition.\n- Enhance omnichannel personalization using AI/ML based on HCP persona/behavior (Next Best Action).\n- Potential label expansions based on ongoing research (e.g., post-MI - EMPACT-MI trial).\n\n---\n\n### • Threats:\n- Aggressive Farxiga commercial tactics (contracting, promotion).\n- GLP-1 RA expansion into HF (STEP-HFpEF data) / CKD (FLOW trial results for Ozempic awaited).\n- Tirzepatide CVOT results potentially strengthening GLP-1 position further.\n- IRA price negotiation outcome impacting Medicare profitability post-2026.\n- Increased payer controls / National formulary exclusions / PBM consolidation.\n- Emergence of novel MOAs in HF/CKD pipeline (e.g., ATTR amyloidosis drugs impacting HF subtypes, novel aldosterone modulators).\n- Patent expiry and generic entry (US LOE projected **2031-2032**, variable by patent).\n\n[FIG]\nTop right corner: Jardiance logo with the word \"empagliflozin\" underneath.\n[/FIG]\n```",

                        "content": "```markdown\nJardiance® (empagliflozin) - Strategic Brand Foundation Dossier FY2025\n=====================================================================\n\n---\n\n**Document Code:** JAR-INT-SBF-FY25-V2.1  \n**Version:** 2.1 (Updated with FY24 Performance)  \n**Date:** 2024-10-26  \n**Status:** Active | **Confidentiality:** BI-Lilly Internal Use Only - Level 4 (Restricted)  \n\n---\n\n### 1. Executive Summary:\n\nJardiance (empagliflozin) is the flagship asset within the BI-Lilly Alliance Cardiovascular-Metabolic (CVM) franchise, holding a market-leading position within the SGLT2 inhibitor class. Its broad label encompassing Type 2 Diabetes (T2D) with CV risk reduction, Heart Failure (HF across LVEF spectrum), and Chronic Kidney Disease (CKD) provides a unique and compelling clinical value proposition. FY2024 performance demonstrated robust growth, particularly driven by HF and the initial CKD launch uptake, exceeding global revenue targets by **3.1%**. However, significant competitive pressure from AstraZeneca's Farxiga and the encroaching GLP-1 RA class (notably Novo Nordisk's semaglutide franchise) necessitates continued strategic focus on differentiation, market access optimization, and flawless execution in FY2025. This dossier serves as the foundational internal reference for strategic planning, marketing execution, and cross-functional alignment for FY2025. Estimated US lifecycle extends to approximately **2031** based on current patent portfolio (subject to ongoing legal review and potential pediatric extensions).\n\n---\n\n### 2. Product Identity & Formulation:\n\n- **Proprietary Name:** Jardiance®\n- **Non-Proprietary Name (INN):** Empagliflozin\n- **Drug Class:** Sodium-Glucose Co-transporter 2 (SGLT2) Inhibitor\n- **Chemical Class:** Glucopyranosyl-substituted benzene derivative\n- **Formulation:** Film-coated oral tablets (Immediate Release)\n- **Excipients:** Lactose monohydrate, microcrystalline cellulose, hydroxypropyl cellulose, croscarmellose sodium, colloidal silicon dioxide, magnesium stearate, hypromellose, titanium dioxide, talc, polyethylene glycol, yellow ferric oxide. (Refer to PI Section 11 for full list).\n- **Available Strengths (US):** 10 mg (pale yellow, round, biconvex, bevel-edged, imprinted with BI logo and 'S10'), 25 mg (pale yellow, oval, biconvex, imprinted with BI logo and 'S25')\n- **Packaging:** Bottles of 30, 90; Hospital Unit Dose Blisters (10x10)\n- **ATC Code:** A10BK03\n- **Initial FDA Approval:** August 1, 2014 (T2D Glycemic Control)\n- **Storage:** Store at 20°C to 25°C (68°F to 77°F); excursions permitted to 15°C to 30°C (59°F to 86°F).\n\n---\n```",

Introduction:\nThis document serves as a primary source of truth defining the operational environment and mandatory compliance rules for promoting Jardiance® (empagliflozin) in key global markets for FY2025. It details market dynamics, payer landscapes, regulatory oversight, and provides explicit operational guardrails (Do's and Don'ts) based on applicable laws, regulations, codes, and internal policies. All promotional concepts, strategies, and materials generated, regardless of method (human or AI-assisted), MUST strictly adhere to these market-specific constraints. Adherence is mandatory; non-compliance carries severe consequences.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Primary Market Focus: United States (US)\n\n#### • Market Overview:\n  - **Size/Scope:** Largest global market (~68% revenue). High prevalence: T2D (~35M), HF (~6.5M), CKD (~37M). Key growth opportunity in HFpEF and diagnosed-but-undertreated CKD (<15% SGLT2i penetration).\n  - **Dynamics:** Intense SGLT2i vs SGLT2i (Farxiga) and SGLT2i vs GLP-1 RA (Semaglutide/Tirzepatide) competition. Guideline adherence (ADA/ACC/AHA/KDIGO) is critical. High promotional environment requires differentiated, compliant messaging.\n\n#### • Payer/Access Environment:\n  - **Structure:** Fragmented: Commercial PBMs (ESI, Caremark, OptumRx), Medicare Part D, Medicaid. Access is highly managed.\n  - **Key Constraints:** \n    - Tier 2/3 placement standard (~85% Commercial lives Tier 3+).\n    - Prior Authorizations (PAs) & Step Therapies (STs - typically metformin first) are common operational hurdles.\n    - IRA Price Negotiation impacts Medicare strategy (MFP effective 2026).\n    - Net price realization averages ~47% of WAC. Patient OOP costs are a barrier; access support programs (co-pay cards, PAPs) are operationally essential.\n\n#### • Regulatory Body & Oversight:\n  - **Primary Body:** FDA/CDER.\n  - **Promotional Oversight:** OPDP (enforces FD&C Act, 21 CFR Part 202).\n  - **Other Oversight:** OIG (Anti-Kickback Statute), DOJ (False Claims Act), CMS (Medicare/Medicaid rules).\n\n---\n\n[FIG]\nIn the upper right corner, the Jardiance® logo appears featuring the brand name with \"empagliflozin\" below it. Avoid euphemisms for risks.\n    - **Prohibition: Efficacy Overstatement:** DO NOT use superlatives (\"best,\" \"safest,\" \"cure,\" \"eliminates risk\"), guarantees, or language implying greater certainty or magnitude of benefit than supported by PI data.\n    - **Prohibition: Unsubstantiated Comparisons:** DO NOT make direct comparative claims vs. competitors (\"superior to,\" \"safer than\") unless based on adequate & well-controlled head-to-head trials **cited within the US PI**. Cross-trial comparisons are presumptively misleading in promotion.\n    - **Prohibition: Misleading Data Representation:** DO NOT use visuals (e.g., truncated graphs) or statistics (e.g., RRR without context) in a way that misrepresents the data or its clinical significance.\n    - **Prohibition: Inconsistent Imagery/Testimonials:** DO NOT use visuals or testimonials depicting scenarios, patient types, or outcomes inconsistent with the PI or that minimize risk.\n\n[FIG]\nTop right of page: Jardiance (empagliflozin) logo.                         "content": "```markdown\n- EMPEROR-P reserved (Trial J AR-HF-002): Randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled trial in 5,988 patients with HFrEF (LVEF >40%), NYHA class II-IV, with or without T2D. Patients received JARDIANCE 10 mg or placebo once daily added to standard HF therapy. Median follow-up 26 months. Primary endpoint: Time to first event of CV death or HHF.\n  Results: JARDIANCE 10 mg significantly reduced the risk of the primary composite endpoint by 21% vs placebo (HR 0.79 [0.69, 0.90], p<0.001). Benefit consistent regardless of T2D status and across LVEF subgroups (>40% to ≥60%).\n\n### 14.3 Chronic Kidney Disease (EMPA-KIDNEY)\n(Trial J AR-CKD-001) Randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled trial in 6,609 patients with CKD at risk for progression (defined by eGFR 20-45 mL/min/1.73 m², or eGFR 45-<90 mL/min/1.73 m² + UACR ≥200 mg/g), with or without T2D (~46% with T2D). Patients received JARDIANCE 10 mg or placebo once daily added to standard care (usually ACEi/ARB). Median follow-up 2.0 years. Primary endpoint: Time to first event of kidney disease progression (defined as ESKD, sustained eGFR decline ≥40%, sustained eGFR <10 mL/min/1.73 m², or renal death) or CV death.\nResults: JARDIANCE 10 mg significantly reduced the risk of the primary composite endpoint by 28% vs placebo (HR 0.72 [0.64, 0.82], p<0.0001). Benefit consistent across key subgroups including baseline eGFR, UACR, and T2D status. JARDIANCE also significantly reduced the risk of hospitalization for any cause by 14% vs placebo (HR 0.86 [0.78, 0.95], p=0.0025).\n\n### 14.4 Glycemic Control in Patients with Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus\nJARDIANCE has been studied as monotherapy and in combination with metformin, sulfonylureas, pioglitazone, DPP-4 inhibitors, and insulin. In patients with T2D, treatment with JARDIANCE produced statistically significant reductions in HbA1c compared with placebo. Reductions in HbA1c were seen across subgroups including age, gender, race, duration of disease, baseline BMI, and baseline renal function (eGFR ≥ 30). JARDIANCE also produced statistically significant reductions in fasting plasma glucose (FPG) and body weight compared to placebo. (Refer to PI Section 14.4 for detailed results of individual trials). A dedicated pediatric trial confirmed efficacy and safety in patients aged 10 years and older.\n\n---\n\n## 16 HOW SUPPLIED/STORAGE AND HANDLING\n\nJARDIANCE (empagliflozin) tablets are available as follows:\n\n- **10 mg tablets**: pale yellow, round, biconvex, bevel-edged, film-coated, debossed with “S10” / BI logo.  \n  - Bottles of 30: NDC 0597-0152-30\n  - Bottles of 90: NDC 0597-0152-90\n  - Hospital Unit Dose (100 tablets; 10x10): NDC 0597-0152-13\n\n- **25 mg tablets**: pale yellow, oval, biconvex, film-coated, debossed with “S25” / BI logo.\n  - Bottles of 30: NDC 0597-0154-30\n  - Bottles of 90: NDC 0597-0154-90\n  - Hospital Unit Dose (100 tablets; 10x10): NDC 0597-0154-13\n```\n",
